Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, then drop some oil of violets or oil of sisamen, and then bring about extraction; and let him sneeze with a condiment, and stop up his nostrils when sneezing comes on, and put around the ear pieces of cloth or wool; and let the ear remain raised.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Fever often comes out through this treatment; and if it does not come out, then a subtle pair of tweezers are used to extract it, and this is its shape:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out with tweezers, that is good; if not, administer extraction with a fine needle of small diameter; and if it does not come out through this, make an iron hook and insert the tip of the hook into the ear canal firmly, and stop the space around the hook with soft wax so that air cannot enter with the hook; then pull it out directly, for often it comes out in this manner as we have said; and if it does not come out in such a way, take some glue and place it on something pointed suitable for this purpose, and put a piece of cotton around it; then press the glue onto the stone or whatever it is, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not come out with all the things we have mentioned, then be quick to split the ear so that the abscess and pain subside, and the method of splitting is that you first bleed the patient's head and extract blood according to its strength, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small split in the root of the ear at the fatty tissue where it depends; and the split should be like a crescent moon, so that you can reach the stone, then remove it according to your ability, and suck it energetically with your mouth; and treat it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if there are grains within it and it swells, then administer extraction; and if it cannot issue out, then administer a .i. spatumile tenve subtle according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and an incision is made on that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this when you think that the grains are moist from the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces; then extract it with subtle tweezers and a sucking device, as we have said, so that the extraction is easy.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the case of water falling into the ear, the patient should use a first-grade sneezing remedy, and pack the ear with old cotton.Car en la piere est grant dolour; et si li maux ne fu par la piere, il fu par le foc ou par l’aygue, si que en li remede de celuy maux li membres ne pot demorer ains qu’il fu eslongiez ou disloiez.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let him lie on the same ear where there is the pain.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it jumps out through the skin, that's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If not, he should take many small stones according to the length of your fingers and heat them gently in the fire. Then put one end of the stone into the ear, and let it come out from another part of his foot; and press down with another stone on the stone which is in the ear. And do not cease doing this with the stones until all the fluid is gone, and so it will all come out. If you see that, he should take a straw, and insert one end into the ear, and heat the other end in the fire until the sharpest straw is burnt; then do the same again with other straws until all the fluid has gone out as we have said regarding the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of an object from the ear, if it is a small object, such as a louse or something similar, treat it as we have said in the previous section. But if it is a large object that can be felt, administer extraction with tweezers; and it is the easiest thing to remove what is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	When extracting worms from the ears, if you treat it as we have described in the section on distilleries, and the treatment does not help, then you should examine the ear in the sun; if any worms appear, you should pluck them out with a pair of delicate tweezers. If none appear, take a piece of wool from where they are formed.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	It is narrow at the bottom and wide at the top.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	Then insert the thinnest end of the needle into the ear according to the amount of pain the patient is experiencing, then suck gently on the needle; do this repeatedly until all the pus comes out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not come out, then pack the ear with cotton as I have said in the case of stones; and if they do not come out as we have described, then administer distillations which the ancients have tried for worm-fighting, and you will find them in the section on distillation treatments; and distil your oils and medicines into the ear using this implement, and make the shape as I have shown you:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And it is made of silver or brass with a narrow end having one small hole and a wider top for distillation; to press the distillation into this instrument, use a well-crafted brass tool, and if you see fit, take a razor and wrap the tip with cotton; then pour in your oil or juice, and what remedies you wish from your medicines into the wool, and let the wool be in the ear; then insert the razor over all the cotton, and gently press your hand so that the oil is distilled into the ear; and the patient will feel it inside, and the distillation should be slightly warmed by fire so that it is not too cold when distilled into the ear.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of earache
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without an opening in their ears; and this same thing happens to men due to earache, or an injury inside the ear. Sometimes these openings occur in the ear itself, so that one cannot see them; and sometimes there is a small wound at the opening of the ear, which can be seen clearly.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore, when the opening occurs and is not visible, it is due to a grievous wound in various parts, and in such cases one should hold the affected ear towards the sun; and look inside: if you see the membrane exposed, then examine it closely to understand its shape.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And it should be sharp and pointy at the front and back, so that it does not cut or injure the ear; if the membrane is due to a wound in the body of the ear, then grasp it with fine tweezers and gently peel away this wound.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the growth is deep in the ear, then take a thin, lightweight razor and heat it slightly in the fire, then apply it to the body of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the itching that the sick person feels when he hears it, pierce slightly and be careful not to damage the ear nerves; then put a tent in the ear according to the size of the hole, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this for several days until the wound is closed; then take a tent and moisten it with rosewater, and sprinkle powdered vitriol on it; and if you see swelling in the ear, it is appropriate to pull out the tent and move another tent moistened with cerot made from rose oil and wax, until the swelling is gone; then treat it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, soak a sponge and cloth in cold water and place it on the ear, and use other treatments that stop the bleeding that are in the remedies for distillations.
de la char des papieres	from the char of papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This herb when it comes in papers of itself when they are moist and are dry, you must extend them with tweezers and pincers, and the root of a spatula; then put ground vitriol on the spot.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if without peeling, then cauterize it with a thin lenticular cautery, and the cauterizer after the incision heals scabs; and many times they return, as long as something remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of hail
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times they come out of the ears things that look like grains in appearance and hardness, and because of this disease is called "hail," and it is a collection of moisture thick on top and bottom; the treatment is such: if the hail moves from one side to another, and it is an easy thing to know, cut it open at the sides, then peel off each part slightly, then take it with tweezers, and crush it.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	if you cannot crush it without piercing the paper, do not worry about hurting the patient; and if the slit is large, sew it up, and treat it until it is healed; and if it is small, do not force it, for the ointment will heal it right away and cause no harm.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the hailstone is descending into the ear towards the upper part, then invert the paper, and grip the hailstone with pincers, and squeeze it from both sides; and if the paper is removed by the incision, that does not matter; and when the hailstone is crushed, apply a poultice of salted water, and clean the wound of any foreign matter until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a grease that is woven into the papers above, and this happens more to children than to adults, and severely to themselves, and they get the catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because their tears hasten to them; and because they lie on their faces, and sleep on top, and their papers are under their eyelids moistened that the inflammation and appearance have covered with exinach which opens in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the area with your fingers and feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the operation is that the patient places his head on the operator's lap; and then take 1 linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity that the exinach occupies in each part, and then place it over the eye; and press with your fingers on both sides so that the exinach gathers within the circle; then cut through the moist skin with a spatula, making an incision no larger than the wound made when opening a vein; and in various cases, the exinach comes out of the incision in the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Take therefore a piece of cloth and hold it between your fingers and thumb, and twist your hand from right to left until it is taut; and be careful not to push into the fissure so that you do not go all the way to the eye, lest you blister it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the skin opens at the beginning of the fissure, gently spread the fissure slightly so that it appears; then extract as we have said, then moisten cloth in vinegar and water, and place on the area, and draw out with a bandage.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such people who grind seal and place it on to corrupt that moisture which remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure the eye until it is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there comes a hot abscess on the area, then treat it with soothing poultices until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	of hair of parchment
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow from papers other than their natural place, and they are enveillit, they harm themselves and bring on various diseases, just as tears, softening of the paper, and albugine, until it leads to their destruction; and there are four ways to treat this: through cauterization with fire, or with a medicine water according to what is mentioned before the chapter on cauterization, and either through incision and stitching or through splints, as I will explain.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You should place the head of the patient in your lap, then hold the paper of the eye in your left hand; if it turns, that is good; if not, then thread a needle with .i. thread; and this should be done from the edge of the paper where the hairs are growing, and draw .i. thread over the entire paper, and return to the razor; then cut into the part under the paper, under the awkward hairs, to the spatumile, copant, from the large larmier to the small one; then remove the thread and place a small tent of cotton and cloth underneath the paper, then sign over the paper a figure of an inch, like a fuelle of mirte, and still it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity you see rising up in every part.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if one has the need, they should apply a large quantity of paper according to how soft the paper is; then make the stich along the two lines that you have marked, and start from the larger wound down to the smaller; and let one of the slits be near the natural hair, in the thickness of a root, then tie the thread in one of the two corners of the heart, then cut it all around; then join the two lips with a single stitch of fine woolen thread using a needle, and wipe away the blood, and let the excess threads dry on the two edges as you see fit; and if not, pay it no heed, then leave the stitch and threads for three or four days; then cure the wound without stitches using dry and constricting things, for the paper will adhere to the wound as it heals, but the stitches are harmful (as the ancients say), and this is a job without fear; and there is another way: you mark the paper with a shape like the leaf of a myrtle, as we have described, with three pointed lobes according to the form given here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut what is above with small scissors evenly according to the form that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the forceps, and the object is not even, then take a needle where it has thread, and pierce it through the middle of the wound; and take another thread alongside the large artery, and the second thread alongside the small one, and bring the threads together evenly between your fingers; then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin above which you have marked, as we have described, then bring the two lips of the wound together by stitching, and heal it until it is cured; and if an abscess comes to your incision, then soothe it with cerate and similar soothing ointments; and sometimes the hairs of the paper are converted: so you must use what we have said about the incision; but the stitching in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of the cane is as follows: you must first turn the paper and place it inside according to what I have said, then make two canes by art, and two thin threads as long as the paper and the width of the spathomyle; then tie two pairs of threads where you hold the threads; then join one and the other subtly above what is on top of the paper of the eye, and pull out the two canes from the two formed parts; and let it be thus for some days, and the skin that was stretched will die and harden and fall off, as long as it falls through itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is delayed, and the incision has some strength, then heal it until it is cured; and when the wound is sewn up, and if the paper is raised, and the hairs do not sting anymore; and this is the form of the two cannings that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of long and wide:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	the operations are such that you pierce a needle and insert a fine and subtle silk thread; then join the heads and tie them together subtly, and let the length of the threads be a palm long; then arrange another fine silk thread in the eye, and tie the end of the thread; then put the patient's head in your hand; and let it be exposed to sunlight so that the operations are declared, for this is a subtle and fine operation, then insert the needle into the root of the hair near the skin, and pierce the paper obliquely until you draw it above the natural hair; then pull out the thread and insert it into the eye of the needle with the natural hair, if there is one or two or three or more; then pull your hand back so that the hairs come out straight through the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the wound is treated and the hair does not come out with it, then you shall treat the wound underneath to the very end that you have prepared for it, until the wound comes out through the opening above and you see it with your eye; then you shall treat the wound and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for 1 or 2 days, until the hair grows back in its place and the flesh grows over it; and if the hair is short, then accompany it with a long hair from the horse's mane, and let it grow with that one which you leave, until it is elongated and then you remove it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the eyelash
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease called "alacratia" or warts comes in the eye, there are two ways of getting it: one natural and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens suddenly from a wound, or from cutting or cauterizing, and in similar ways.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the way to treat it is that you split the sore, and pull back its edges, and put in tents of linen, and leave it until it heals; and you must not use anything in its treatment which would dry and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do that, the disease will return worse than before; but work with softening things, such as fenugreek; and rosewater or altee water, and linseed cooked in some of the oils, and ointments of dissolved diaquilon, and wrap it up in a tent, and treat it thus.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the goal of your treatment is that you take care that it does not heal according to the form that it was before; and these works which we have said are not remedies for this disease, so that it does not return according to the form that it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease, which is deep inside, is truly called "axacrati", and it is both natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	Accidents come from wounds and cuts and cautery and similar things; the way to treat them is to take a needle with a double thread, and pierce it through the flesh, and make it go out of the left eyebrow so that the thread goes into both sides of the face; then the flesh is pulled up above the needle, and the cup is made very wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the wound returns as it should be, that is good; if not, then take a razor and put it in the cut, and turn the flesh, and make two cuts inside the wound; and let the sides of both cuts be the two angles of the incision you have made, so that when they are stitched together, the shape is like the shape of a letter which has no "I griesche"; then remove this flesh, according to the quantity that its sides are cut under, from what follows the wound, then join the two torn parts and sew them with a thread of wool; then treat it as we have said with softening medicines and bandages until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from a split or stitch or cautery, then you should make a plain split underneath the hair of the scalp, and according to what is mentioned above; then unsheathe between the two lips of a tent, as I have said; and the operation should be performed according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise master prepares an instrument with all his power, how he makes the figure return to its natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what he needs in terms of operation and instruments in various dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	suddenly from the scalp
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this splitting occurs in the hands of men in such a way that the scalp above is separated from the white of the eye, and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you should therefore insert the point of a razor underneath the scalp, and lift it up; and stretch it with tweezers, until you grip what is open to the subtile spatula, which is neither too round nor too sharp, so that the patient cannot bear that the too-sharp spatula pierces the eye; and make your incision, by which you peel away this union, lightly, so that the scalp returns according to its natural shape; and all of this union is healed, and they sometimes create an ulcer in the eye, and raise it with warm water, and with a bandage; then place a tent of linen between the scalp and the eye, and place wet wool on the eye; and after the third day, use the bandage and soothing things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	You should know that the nail comes in two forms: one is nerveous and resembles a hard cyst; the other is not nerveous but resembles congealed white moisture, which, when touched with iron and pinched, cannot be pierced by any means; both kinds begin at the inner corner of the eye, grow little by little, and cover the entire sight, light, and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of incision is that the patient places his head over yours, then he opens his eyes; you hold the piece of paper in your hand, then grip the nail with tweezers at the cuticle and lift it up; next, take a needle, thread a horsehair, or cow's hair, or ox hair through it, double the tip of the needle over, insert it into the nail, tie the nail with a thread, and lift it up; then scrape along the side of the nail that follows the eyelid all the way to the tear gland, being careful to not pierce the tear duct; sometimes, only the cuticle and thread are needed, as mentioned; then scrape along the soft tissue around the tear gland, taking care not to damage the tear duct with the incision.
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful not to touch the fleshy membrane and rupture it, nor pierce the tear gland; after the incision, apply a little powdered quicklime to the eye, and a collar made of linseed oil, and leave it on until the next day; then treat it as needed until it heals.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nervous and you cannot push in the needle, and the hooked pins cannot enter, many times this kind of nail has been cured by medicines; and it heals as I have described in the division, and if you see it covered, then work the eye of the malady, and take the spatula gently with a small hook according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And lift the nail gently, and if you see that it does not lessen and the pus continues to come out, then distill from your mouth into the eye a collar made of litharge and red collar, and if it is ground, and stop the eye until the next day; then resume the other work according to this same action, until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If there is no contrary thing in the eye, such as a hot abscess, then treat it with milk, and first cure the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume the work as before, until it is healed.Se li ungle est vairons ou si grant, et ne puet gueres estre curé, adonques le tranche selonc la forme de l’ungle, et le traie hors dou pie; puis tache l’ungle s’il est chaut, et met sus dou baume de colofonia et d’uncina de vairons et de pluyer, et le retrempe en l’oil dou mal.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the nail is very large and cannot be cured easily, then cut it according to the shape of the nail, and pull it out from the toe; then burn the nail if it is hot, and put on balsam of colophony and of the nail and of vitriol, and re-drip into the eye of the malady.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows above the eyeball
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	In some men, red pustules sometimes emerge on the eyelids, covering the eyelid and pressing down on the eyelashes; they resemble a rose on a column. The treatment is for the patient to place his head on your lap, then you work on the eyelids, and carefully cut away all the pus to the bone, holding it firmly in place. Then cut through the first pustule, and continue cutting away at the root until the end; be careful not to damage the eye during this process. The incision should be made with a spatulum, as described earlier for the fingernail incision, using gentle pressure to remove the pus, as demonstrated in this chapter. Once the incision is complete and all the pus has been removed, apply oil of sea-holly or distil red vitriol and similar corrosive medicines onto the eye; then place a cotton pad soaked in egg white over the eye to secure it and encourage a hot abscess. If nothing remains, and the white part of the eye turns red, indicating a hot abscess, leave the eye alone and treat the abscess with soothing remedies for hot abscesses. Then return to treating the eye until it is healed, and do the same for any other pustules that develop in the eye in this way.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	However, you should always use the natural method for curing weak eyes, and the accidental method for strong eyes; and do not use your hand in either treatment until you see that this member is suffering from the other treatment.
des voines des eulz	of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Thus are red veins which are covered over the eye, and they obscure one's vision and weaken the eye all day long.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Thus, the first thing you must do is examine the eye to see if it is affected by this condition and there is no other disease present; then have the patient tilt his head back and gently squeeze those veins all along their length according to your judgment, taking care to use a gentle touch.
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And massage in circles going downward on one side of the eye according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then press those veins gently, and draw out the blood little by little, hour after hour, until you see the veins drawn away from the eye; but be careful not to hurt the eye with the points of your fingers, and do this work at noon in the sunlight, and be very diligent in your task so that you do not leave any of the veins untouched. And when you have finished, instil a mixture of green and red collyrium into the eye to purify what remains of the redness.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you do not have the power to pull out all of this in that hour, then make a plaster over the eye with things that soothe the pain of the eyes, and let it be for several days until the pain is appeased and assured of a hot abscess; then begin again according to the manner set forth above until he is healed; and that is the form of strength:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the eye fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	Look carefully at the "arissati" fistula: when you heal it with cautery and medicine with a hot fire according to what I have said before, and it is not healed, there is an issue in it that you split open over the abscess, where it should remain, and draw out all the moisture until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed and you will see the corruption and blackness, then you will use the instrument again, of which there is the form; and it is called a  "aspre chief", and it should be made to be sharp at one end, and punctured like a file as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place it over the site of the corrupt bone, then turn it between your fingers, and press your hand slightly until you feel that the corruption has been removed; do this a few times, then restore the site with drying medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the eye is cured, and there are no other signs of illness apart from the fistula, then you should simply treat it according to the instructions given earlier in this text; but if there are other issues, or if the fistula persists for 40 days without healing, causing discomfort, then you must operate a second time with an iron instrument and sharp medicines; when the eye is open again, insert the iron tool gently as described before, making sure the iron has three angles, and the shaft is thinned at the end so that it can reach the eye easily:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	then he puts it on the bone of the ear, and pulls his hand away from the eye a little, then returns to press the bore all the way through the bone until he feels the patient's pulse through it; and then he packs the wound with dry medicine as I have taught you, and when the flesh heals and hardens, he inspects the pulse in the hand; this is an easier procedure for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	from the opening of the eye:
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are fully open all around and there is no disturbance to the eye or diminution, then you should ligature the patient; then heal, then place leeches or suckers without piercing to draw out, then apply a poultice on top made from aconite and aloe and incense and sarcocolla, and then bind the eye, using bandages and linen; the manner of the linen is that you fold linen very softly, and double each one into four, and then place one on top of another according to the quantity that the eye needs; then bind it tightly from above with a firm bandage, and then restart the leeches to draw out without piercing; then remove the leeches and leave the eye bound day and night, and if the ligature softens, then you should tighten it greatly; then remove the ligature after a day and a night, and if you see the eye healing, that is good; if not, then restart the poultice and the linen and the ligature and the leeches until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	from the rupture of woven fabric
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions occur in woven fabric, then it opens and appears like a grain of resin, and is frightening to see; therefore, if you see it covered, the work is such that you insert a needle into the root of the part below up to the part above, then insert another needle where there is a double thread of the part of the armhole; and pierce it, and leave the first needle according to its position; then cover the place of the double thread and tie one part of the fabric around, and tighten it well, then remove the needle and apply a poultice made from a soft egg yolk on top of the eye; and leave it until the thread breaks with the fabric, then cure the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is restricted by the fabric in a circle of linen, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes give great pain, then pierce them with a sharp needle which comes from the back of the eye, and dry out the moist white part and lower the eyes, and put them in as far as they will go; then pull on them until they are healthy.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the back of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease called «alcunnati» is nothing but a swelling in the eye, resembling descending pus, but it is not pus; and the way to diagnose it is to make the patient sit upright and still, then take his head in your hands and move it until you see the swelling come up to your eyes; then it should be treated, and the light turned away from him so that he can see things as he used to; and if the swelling does not go down, know that it is pus, but if the descending swelling is not as we have described.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you cause the patient to sit between your hands, then take the spatulum and insert it under the horny membrane at the edge of the conjunctiva with the horny membrane and the cornea, until the sac is burst; and when it has been discharged, distill into the eye warm water mixed with honey, or water in which fenugreek and honey have been boiled; then let it be treated with other remedies until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the eye waters
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have already discussed the appearances of diseases in the division, and what is needed to pierce them; now act according to the patient's condition.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	You should cause the patient to sit between your hands, facing away from the light so that the sun does not hurt his eyes, and then press the healthy eye shut very tightly; then take the paper for the eye in your left hand if the eye is on the left, or in your right hand if it is on the right; then hold in your right hand, if the eye is on the left, the instrument called 'almagda', or in your left hand if the eye is on the right; then place the tip of the instrument alongside the cornea through that white part of the eye where the tear duct emerges, and push the instrument called 'almagda' gently and twist your hand so that it pierces into the white part of the eye, and you will feel the almagda reach the empty space; the depth of the passage of the almagda should be equal to the distance from the pupil to the edge of the iris; this is the cornea of the eye; then you will see the bone through the paper due to the clarity of the horny membrane, and then push the instrument to where the water is, then express it beneath one membrane after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	if the pain comes now, let the patient see the instrument before him.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After rest for a little, if the pain comes again, push out the blood with the instrument, and when it is stuck and does not flow, gently withdraw the almagda by turning your hand a little; then put in a little gem-stone, and remove this from the eye inside.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then insert into the eye wool or linen moistened in rosewater and an abundance of egg yolk, and bind it with clean bandages.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those of our time, put on a poultice of ground comfrey mixed with an abundance of egg yolk.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are some people whose eyes are too hard, then you should take the instrument called  "alberit", which has this shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And so the conjunctiva only, and do not go too deep, but make the cut fine, then insert the almagda as we have said; and when the treatment is complete, prepare for the patient a dark bed, in which he sleeps on his back in a dark place; and let him be free of all movement, and eat light foods, and do not move his head or to the right or left, and tie him according to his disposition for three days; then untie him in that same dark house, and test his vision, and show him some things, and then put the bandage back on for seven days; and you must not do this during the hour of the treatment or after an incision now, but it is necessary to alleviate this so that the blood flows rapidly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When these eye abscesses arise, you must release the eye before the seventh day and apply a remedy for abscesses; and when it is soothed, then loosen the eyelid and place a gold ring over it to cover any sore, and then keep it in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then exit the house a little at a time, and return to your normal routine; and know that no disciple should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us from the Land of Iraq, who told us that in his country they pierce with alum, and suck out the water, but I have never seen anyone doing this in our land, nor have I read about it in books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the similitudes of the forms of almagest, because those who do not know them may see them; and they are properly made of brass.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And let the heads of these be of the same subtlety, and the points in three angles.
de la char sor le neis	through the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	At times, various types of warts grow on the body, some resembling scorpions with many feet; and others have a wart with a hollow center of a dark color, and another type is a wart with a hollow center of a fair color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	For the type of wart that is hollow and not raised, one must have the patient stand between your hands facing the sun; open his nostrils, and pour the oil onto the warts, pulling them out; then apply what you can bear with a thin spatula from one side, until you know the wart has been entirely removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	If something remains which cannot be removed, then open it with a sharp instrument lightly so that nothing remains; and if without swelling, or an abscess forms, then lanced as appropriate; and if malignant abscesses form, then hasten to cauterize them until the pus is drained and all the corruption is removed, then apply cold water, or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If it works on the nose and moisture reaches the palate, know that it is healthy; and if moisture does not pass through as it should, know that there is rotten flesh in the bone above, which the instruments cannot reach: therefore you must insert a thick thread of linen, and let it be knotted with our fingers, and let there be between each knot the width of a finger or less; and put the patient's end of the thread into his nose to his ability, and pull it through with scent until it comes out of the nose into the mouth; and children often do this in schools, and it is an easy thing for anyone who wants to do it; then hold the end that comes out of the nose in one hand, and the other end that comes out of the mouth in the other hand, and pull them apart gently while feeling the thread with your fingers.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this until you know that the night has corrupted the flesh, then draw out the thread, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back into the nose as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointment corrodes all that remains of the flesh; and then put a plug of lead into the nose for several days until it is healed, and if he needs dry medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to cleanse the head, with which one distils oils and medicines into the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	It should be made of silver or brass, in the shape of an open lamp, like a tube, and with a handle to control it; and if you wish, make a closed tube, and fill it with medicine to cleanse the ears; and there should be a small handle at the end for holding it while heating the oil or any other liquid.
de la char sor le neis	through the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	many times a disease called "telul" arises at the top of the nose; it grows and becomes large, so that it is visible to the eye. Therefore, you should treat it at first, and remove all of it, then place upon it a cautery or burning medicine. If one delays in treating it until it has become large, then be wary if it is hard, dark in color, and insensate: do not touch it with iron, for it is an abscess. For when one treats it, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is due to a superficial touch, not from deep color, and you see that one can completely cover it, then evacuates the patient and treat the site with dry and constricting substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution of continuity comes in any of these cartilage openings, it benefits little except in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore when this happens to anyone, one must look to see if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then bring the two lips together with a stitch, then treat it until it is healed; and if the lips are torn on both sides, then you must scrape all parts of their flesh until they heal, then bring the two lips together with a stitch, tighten them, and powder with dragon's blood powder and ground incense; and put a piece of strong plaster or other binding plaster over the powders, leave it to heal by itself, then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of sewing is that you assemble the needle: either by needle, as we have said in the sewing of the belly; or by thread, as I have made you aware.
des apostemes des levres	of lip abscesses
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At home on the lips there are hard abscesses, resembling grains of wheat, small and large; therefore you should cut into the lip, and pierce each pustule with pincers, and scrape out each one; then apply powdered vitriol after making an incision, until the blood is stopped; then use a poultice of garlic, and treat the area with dry remedies until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of gum pain
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times a growth arises on the gums, which the ancients call "albus"; you should hold it with tweezers, cut at its root, and let the blood or pus flow out; then place ground vitriol, or other restraining and drying powders, over the site; if the growth returns after the incision, and this often happens, cut it again and cauterize it; if it does not return after cautery, that is the form for treating an abscess.
des sordens	of the ears, and of the eyes, and of the nose, and of the throat, and of the mouth, and of the gums, and of the teeth, and of the tongue, and of the palates, and of the head, and of the brain, and of the neck, and of the collar bones, and of the shoulders, and of the armpits, and of the arms, and of the elbows, and of the wrists, and of the hands, and of the fingers.
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are gathered at the roots of the teeth, in the mouth between the gums, scabs that are unsightly and rough; and sometimes the teeth are black and yellow and wormy, when corruption comes to the gum, and they stink; so you should make the patient hold his head in your hands, and press his gums with your thumb, and pull the teeth or the scabs until nothing remains; and thus do the same for blackness and greenness, and yellowness and other discoloration, until they are cleaned; and if one pulls out what is at the first cause, that is good; if not, then repeat it again on the second day and the third, until you have pulled everything out; and know that teeth require various forms of instruments for pulling, according to what the work demonstrates, so that the instrument used to pull out teeth have different forms from those used to pull between the teeth; and these forms and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When you treat a toothache and draw it out, take as long as you can, for this must not be done quickly; for the tooth is a very sensitive substance until there is no more excuse for drawing it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then, when the patient is forced to pull, you must be certain of the tooth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain torments the patient and believes it is in a sound tooth, and forces the good tooth to be pulled; and yet the pain does not depart from him because of this, as long as the evil tooth remains, for we have already seen this happen with these patients. And when you are quite certain of the decayed tooth, you must scrape around the tooth with a sharp instrument to drive away the gum in every part; then move it with your fingers or with fine tweezers, little by little, until it is well loosened; then grip it firmly with the tweezers.
