And let the head of the patient be between your knees, and hold him so that he does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	Afterwards, pull out the tooth carefully without breaking it, and if it does not come out, take one of these instruments and insert it into each side gently, then move it as before.And when he has pulled out the tooth, let him stop the bleeding with a piece of sponge or some such thing.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the teeth are pierced and eaten away, you must fill the holes with pieces of cloth, and gently hold them tight with tweezers so they do not break while being held; and it is necessary to work carefully around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be careful that you do not break it and leave a piece behind, for then the pain will be worse due to the root's maliciousness.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And beware of doing as ignorant healers do, who in their haste and arrogance sometimes break the tooth, not heeding what we have told you; but sometimes they bring about a great illness due to the roots that remain, or by breaking the tooth, as we have often seen. And when the tooth is pulled, wash the area with wine or garlic and salt; and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, apply powdered vitriol to the site; and if this does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of instruments with which the teeth are pulled first should have long points and thick handles so they do not break when you pull on the tooth. And these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be made of strong metal so that they do not bend when pulling, and they should have teeth to hold the gums.
de la racine des dens	of the roots of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains in place, you must put wet cotton on the area for a day or two.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the area is softened; then put in the tweezers known as "algefri", which make the shoulder look like a sore; and inside they are made like a file, and this is their shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these tweezers, then you must uncover the flesh all around the root, and insert the instrument called "althali", that is to say, a spatula, of which this is the shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	It should be strong and wide so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out through this, that is good; if not, then use all the instruments, of which the forms come below:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one uses this instrument which has two branches, of which this is the shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools that are in the reason of teeth, and of this instrument which resembles large tweezers, of which this is the shape:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let this instrument be outside so that it does not break, and know that there are many instruments of teeth; and also other instruments which are not counted; and the wise subtle masters find their own instrument by themselves according to what their works and the disease show them, because there are many diseases in which the ancients did not teach an instrument due to the diversity of others; and if it does not break in the cart or other bones, but protrudes, then he looks for the instruments that he needs, that I have told you about, and helps with gestures, from which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and well-fitting to hold the bone so that it does not slip, but he can hold and remove it; and then restore the site with appropriate medicines, and if there is protuberance in the bone, and it is small, then treat it with this instrument.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to the natural structure of the body, and its shape is ugly, especially in virgin women, then you should know if the tooth is new after the tooth, and is not in the right place, and cannot be filed or ground down; then cut it off; and if there is an air bubble with the tooth, then take this instrument of which the form is like a small beak, and let it be made of iron sharpened at the tip:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the gum shrinks a little bit each day because of the hardness of the tooth and so that you do not move the others, and if it is apparent that one can file it, then file it with an ivory file like this is the shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and is also like the file with which we make needles; and file the tooth a little bit each day lightly, so that it does not move until it fits; then smooth it at the end with any rasp, and if the tooth is too sharp and cuts the tongue, then file the sharpness so that it is even and does not cut the tongue or corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth is loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front teeth protrude, either from biting or falling, and the patient cannot press on what he eats without defecating, and you have treated them with constricting medicines to no avail; then they must be restrained with a gold wire, for silver wire turns green and rots, but gold never moves; and the wire should be neither too thin nor too thick, according to the amount of space between the teeth. And if you see the teeth tilting, take the wire and wrap it double between the two healthy teeth, then put the shoulder between the teeth, if there is one or more, until you come to bleeding at the healthy tooth on the other side; then begin covering again until you reach the part where you started, and strain your hand gently and bleedingly, so that it does not move. And your aim should be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then grasp the teeth with tweezers, and bring them together, and fit them between the healthy teeth, and place it so that it does not cut the tongue; then leave it thus tightly as long as it can stay, and if it comes loose, or the threads break, then hold it with another thread; let it remain and serve in this way for its entire life, and this is the form of the teeth and the arrangement of the two healthy teeth, and the two diseased ones, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth falls out, it is replaced in its place, little by little, as we have said; and no one who is not wise and careful should attempt this, and sometimes the shape of a tooth from a cow's bone is made, and placed in the place where there is a defect, and bound as we have said, and it remains and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the line on the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Sometimes this ligament which comes under the tongue, is present from birth; or by accident of a wound; and the treatment is such that you open the mouth of the patient, and places his head in yours, and holds his tongue; then grasp the nervous ligament with forceps, as far as the tongue is separated from its bed, and if there is hardening or a lump, and this is due to a wound, then cut it with scissors and grasp the ligament with forceps; and be careful that the cut is not too deep, so as not to reach the artery which is underneath; and when you have done, raise the area with rosewater and garlic, or cold water, then place under the tongue a tent of linen; and apply a cautery to the patient every night, so that the sutures do not stick together.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if blood oozes out, then apply powdered vitriol over the area; and if the wound bleeds, then cauterize it with a slow-burning cautery, which is good for this purpose; then treat it with other remedies until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it is dark colored or black and hard, and the patient does not feel any pain, then do not touch it, as it is a ulcer; and if it is inclined towards gangrene, and there is moisture, cut it from the side with a sharp spatula, and loosen it from both sides; and if bleeding occurs due to your action, apply crushed vitriol until it stops, then return to your treatment, pulling out all the way, then apply a mixture of garlic and vinegar, and clean the wound further until it heals. Then apply a poultice of garlic and vinegar to the affected area, and clean the wound further until it is completely healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses in the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes there are growths in the throat called 'godath', and they are properly called 'almonds'; when you treat them, as we have said in the section on their nature, if they are not healed, then take care: if they are hard abscesses of small size and light color, do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, so that there is no blood flow; but let it be until it is ripe, and then you will burst it, or it will burst by itself; and if it is of a white color, soft, and the root is thin, have an instrument to cut, but first examine whether the abscess is calm and peaceful.Et s’il est dur et il rompt par soi, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout; et si li sangs vaint par la fente, si met sor l’enduit qui se fait sor les apostemes dures.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then have the patient sit facing the sun, with his head in your shadow, and open his mouth wide, and let the servant hold his jaw between their hands, and press his tongue down to the bottom of the instrument, from which the shape is taken; it should be made of thin silver or brass like a knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	As you press the tongue with this instrument, you will see the abscess; then take a pair of forceps and insert it into the tonsil, pulling it out as far as possible. Remove any threads from the wound with the forceps, then cover the wound with the cautery instrument again, which has a pointed shape, resembling a needle; the instrument should be curved on one side and straight on the other, and very sharp, made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument available, you can use tweezers, which have a similar shape:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And it is pointed on one side and blunt on the other; and when you have lanced one of the glands, lance the other according to the same method, and after the incision gargle the patient with warm water, and water and garlic, and if there is a discharge of blood, gargle the patient with water or cooked pomegranate peels, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding stops; then cure it until it is healed; and sometimes other abscesses besides the two glands form in the throat, so lance them thus as the two glands were lanced.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was inside her throat, namely a small one; and it had closed up her entire throat so that the woman could not breathe through the passageway which was blocked, and she could not eat or drink, and would have died if it had continued for another day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so high that it had pushed out two little bumps through the nostril holes.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I quickly then, stuck in one fingernail, then drew it out and took a large piece of bowels; then I did the same on the other nostril hole and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; after that, I stuck the nail into the abscess, and scooped out a portion, and only a little blood came out; thus was the passageway of the throat cleared for the woman, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I continued to cut this abscess for a long time; and the abscess grew again, filling up the space that I had emptied, so that it became very big; therefore, I lanced it and cauterized it inside her throat; thus it remained without growing; and I left these parts, and she was in God's hands after me.
de l’uve	of the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the eye descends to the lid, and it is swollen and it is long, it is called 'perpendicular'; and if it is fat and round beneath, it is called an 'eye'.
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it has been treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, and you see that the abscess is quieted, and it is subtle, then you should cover it; and if it is round and gathered and not long, and it is blood-red or flesh-colored or black, then you should avoid cutting into it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it according to the way that I have said, of its whiteness and length, you should cause the patient to sit facing the sun, and press his tongue against the instrument which we have mentioned earlier; then insert the needle into the eye, and draw it out underneath, and cover it at the place of the II instruments that I mentioned in the incision of the II almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And you must not cover anything beyond the natural limit; for if you cover more, it weighs down the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said about the incision of the two testes, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient fears covering, you should use an anaesthetic for the pain of cauterisation.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	The method of the cautery is for acute disease.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient should put his head into your healthy hand, and then press his tongue against the instrument we have described in the chapter on cautery, and breathe in sharp breaths, so that it is not too slow or too fast; and use the implement of which this is the shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	and has a handle at the top where one puts the medication, like the handle of a spoon, and places the instrument with all the medication on it over the eye; and the patient should lie on his side, so that the saliva and mucus flow from his mouth due to the medication inside, so that it does not descend into the throat and choke him; then hold your hand over the medication and press it onto the eye for the duration of half an hour, until you see it become numb and the bites of the medication calm down. And if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument into the eye all the way to the cotton, so that the cotton adheres to the eye; and do this often until the cautery is complete, then let it dry and fall off after four or five days. And if you need to re-administer the cautery of the medication, then do so, and after the cautery, wash around the eye with cold water, and treat it with gargles until it heals.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This treatment is safer than incision or cautery; if it is treated with fumigation according to this method, take calamine and hyssop and marjoram and rue and chamomile and avens and similar herbs, and assemble all or some of them in one pot, and add garlic, and let it boil. And the pot should be well glazed with strong clay, and in the pot there should be one instrument shaped according to this method:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be made of silver or brass, and one of the ends put into the mouth of the patient so that the vapour rises to the eye through the canal until the eye is numbed; afterwards, repeat often until the eye dries, and take care not to do this at the beginning of the formation of a hot abscess, for various things can happen; and also not to do this beyond the decline of a hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a cane and put an egg-shell inside the end so that the patient's mouth is not too hot; for the egg-shell will not let the vapour harm the mouth, and it is a beneficial treatment together with salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times a fish bone or spine, or some object, becomes stuck in the throat; so you must pull out what you can see and press the tongue against the sun with all the instrument, so that you can move the object; and what does not appear to you and is lodged in the throat, you should make the patient vomit as long as the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps the object will come out through vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or a dry piece of bread; and attach a thread to the sponge, and then swallow it; and when it comes to the spot, it will stick, and then you can pull it out; and if it does not come out through what we have said, take an instrument of lead according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be bent at the end so that it can more easily enter the throat, and have the end lifted up high; and beware of touching the epiglottis, so that it does not choke him, nor push the bone inside; and move as long as the patient swallows the instrument, so that he can move the object; then he swallows it down, or pulls it out with the instrument equally, until it is out.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the blood of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Sometimes the treatment is with blood-letting, as I have said in the division, through the cure of medicines; and when that does not help, then look into the throat of the patient facing the sun, then press his tongue with the instrument I have described to you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see blood, draw it out with a small hook, or with fine tweezers that are suitable for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if that does not work, take a chisel-like cane and put it into the throat of the patient, then put the end of the cane in hot iron, and do this often.Et se le malaide est en la gueule, si traie la sansue a leu; et s’il ne peut avoir l’estrument, si prend une caine et met dedens I fer chaut, puis le boute en la gueule, et fai ce sovent a leu.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient has fever all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	then take full water in a glass, open the mouth, and spray it in without swallowing, and move it with his hand often; and as soon as he feels the water, he will spit it out.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not spit as we have said, then smoke the patient with assafetida, using the instrument that I described for smoking out the throat; do this many times, because it will spit out without bleeding.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the way to smoke it is to put burning charcoal in a pot, and cover it with a perforated lid, and insert the instrument through the hole; then spray in the smoke, and the patient puts his throat into his mouth, and closes his mouth so that none of the smoke escapes, but goes to the blood; and now the blood will come out, and if it does not, then repeat the smoking many times; and let the patient suffer thirst, eat salty and sour things, and do not drink water; and then it will be necessary for him to spit it out through this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the instrument used to treat hemorrhoids resembles, when it can be seen, bent tongs designed to enter the throat; it also resembles a doctor's beak and has the roughness of a file so that it cannot let go of what it grasps. And here is its form:
li chapistres des apostemes	for abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	There are many kinds of abscesses, according to what memory brings hereafter from one and another in this book, and they differ in penetration and size; and there are two ways in which they occur, one being in their appearance themselves, and the other in what they contain.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is because of the places where they are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses in the head are different from those in the fundament, and the abscesses in fleshy places are different from those that come in joints, and each has its own treatment.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And in some abscesses one must not pierce as long as the bowels are healthy according to their completion; and there are some that one must pierce when they have become crusted, and yet they do not die according to their completion, like abscesses that are near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	Because when abscesses come from these joints, and are left until they become purulent around the edges, by chance the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, which causes contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Or the abscess is by the principal member, and if you delay perforation until it is mature, it will harm the principal member; or it is by the fundament, then one should pierce it in such a way that it may be cured without digestion being completed, except for that which is by the fundament, which should not be allowed to ripen inside but should be elongated and cured, and a fistula will come from it, and it will not heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you must know the time of the piercing of the abscess which is dead according to its maturity, and that is when the pain is appeased, and the departing of the fever, and the lessening of the pain and redness, and the softening and sharpening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and you must make the piercing at the most dependent part of the abscess, and where it appears soft; and the piercing should be made deep in the body, and if the abscesses are on the hands or feet, or in joints, and on nerves, and arteries, and in all places alike where there is no fold.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those who bend, according to that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when the abscess is in a fleshy place, it is better to let the perforation be until it is confirmed in completed digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it before that, the body is drawn out, and it is full of much filth, and perhaps hardens the lips and the depths within him.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if to any abscess that are pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the member needs.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And one must treat small abscesses with small holes, and large abscesses with large holes, and many slits according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses that one should cut out the core, and cover it; when it has become as soft as rags, and is deadened, one must do as one does with blisters: and there are some that split into three angles, and some that one covers just like a fir tree, and others that have one round incision, and other incisions and similar coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who have no head, as with a superficial abscess, you must pierce it plainly; and when the abscess is large, and it has drawn a great bowstring, and you pierce it, do not draw out the entire bowstring in that hour, but draw out a part of it; then stop the abscess until the next day, then draw out something again from the other side; do this many times, little by little, until the bowstring is fully released; likewise if the patient is of weak constitution, or a woman carrying a child, or a small child, or an old decrepit man.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the pus may spurt out with the release of the bowstring, and the patient may die without your realizing it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, approach this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced the abscess, wash the wound, and examine if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a plain cut, apply bandages of linen or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess with many openings, you should tie a tent in each opening so that they come together; and if you have cut into the abscess and exposed part of the skin, and cleaned it around, you should fill it with old cotton or linseed without moisture, and bandage it for three days; then remove the bandage and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs in your work, bring cold water and ease it, and moisten the cloth, and place it over the bleeding area many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding persists, apply treatment and care, and the powders that I mentioned with my own hands in this book; and if it is during the winter, and the area is very nervous, then you should place wet tents and cloths soaked in warm wine and oil over it; and if it is in the summer, and the area is fleshy, then you should place wet cloths soaked in water and oil, or in cool wine and oil, for a third of a day, as we have said; then loosen the abscess, wash and treat it, as it should be, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	Now you should understand, in general, the treatment of abscesses. I have told you how to proceed before treating abscesses, and you can find this chapter now.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	From the skin of the head come small abscesses, and they are caused by lice, just like the nits on a goose, and there are many variations of them.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are fatty and smooth where there is moisture just as with pulses; and there are some that are hard and stony in texture, and there is no doubt if the artery does not cause contrary effects.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the throat is that you should try with every instrument called "forceps", from which the form comes afterwards, whatever it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, they force it out from above.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is expelled, they scorch without leaving anything of the skin that contains the moisture, for it will return again if something is left behind; then plunge cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; if not, in water and salt, and apply it to the wound and let it be until the next day, and those who remain during the night will recover.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then resume the cotton, as before, on the second day and the third, until you know that it will not remain overnight; then heal the wound with ointment that is appropriate, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess contains pus and fat, then open it according to this form, from the top; and cut your fingernails, and scrape off all the scabs, and apply all your treatment to drawing out the pus under the skin; and if the artery pulsates in a contrary fashion, then do what I have told you after.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do this for an abscess that is full of pus, cutting and treating it as I have said.Et se li apostemes ne veut pas faire evacuation de l’escorche, si li cope selonc ceste forme; et si li sainz vout a la mort, si le cop en la forme que je t’ai dit avant.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the incision on the abscess of stone and moisture, it is lighter, because they are of little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if any of these abscesses there is no moisture, and some were the abscesses that I copied from the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess as hard as a stone, rough and white, and could not be broken; and if anyone had burst them, they would have made a wound just like a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming to the head, other than those that come to the heads of children and the roots of the ears, the opening should be at the most dependent location, so that the bowels can exit; and treat them as appropriate.
des scrophules	of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times abscesses come to the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes they come elsewhere in the body, and they are large, and some are intertwined with each other.Et li clous des enfans, si com il convient, il fuet boine chose que les cure, et que les fiet boines curaties; car s’il adonques l’enfaunt ne morist pas de la maladye qui le veniet, si morist par la malcuratie; car il est grant danger as enfans qui sont en ceste maladye.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly within its coat, as the nodule and abscess of the head, as we have said; and there are many similar scrofulas.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and others that are malignant and will not respond to treatment.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	For those that you see are of good disposition for cauterization, and resemble the color of the body, and are flat on each side and not raised on the nerves or artery or duct, and is not deep; you should cut it from above, and scrape off each part, and be careful that you do not cut the nerve or vein, and do not use too much force, or else the hand will shake, and do not go too far, so that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it will not let you work, then put crushed vitriol or some powder that stops bleeding into the wound, and compress the wound; and leave it until the abscess is subdued, and the wound softened, and begins to suppurate.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the bleeding is stopped, return to your work, completing it; then examine with your finger if any small scrofula remains, cut and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein at the root of the scrofula, you should not cut that scrofula in its root but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it drop without harm; then treat the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, and then heal it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut the whole scrofula, you should bring together the two lips of the wound and sew them now so that no surplus remains due to the size of the scrofula.Et si li sans ne voulent point estainchir, si met en la voinne vitriole broiet, ou autre poudres qui contengent sang, et li estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et li membres amolisiz, et comence a porrir.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	then you must understand to cover the root of it, and draw it out, and cut it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrophules that hold superfluity, pierce where it appears dead; and pierce it thus as the one before was said, depending on it, then treat it with tenting along with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts that which is remained of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, then cure it with ointment encrusting flesh, until it is healed.
de squinance	of scrofula
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients wrote and spoke of throat surgery; but I have never seen it done in our land, and this is the script of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those with scrofula, it is necessary to open the flap of the throat, called the 'epiglottis'; and this should be done gently, for all the veins and the lymph node are affected by the disease, whether the abscess is hot in the mouth, or in the throat, or in both armpits.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the lymph node channel, one must cover the epiglottis to avoid the danger that comes from strangulation.Il conviant aussi que li medecins sache le goute et le sentour de la maladie; car onque il n’i a pas bon sanz sa science.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we want to split the epiglottis, we must split it below the three circles or four, a little split across, between the two circles, or by the amount of the split from the soft palate; and those parts that are suitable for the splitting of the epiglottis so that there is no flesh in it, and the vessels are long within.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the masters are fearful, they should stretch the skin of the throat to the Adam's apple, then split the windpipe until it reaches the larynx; and avoid the blood vessels, if you see anything, and then close the wound, as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the windpipe at the larynx, which jumps out through the place that is broken, and by the defect in the voice; and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed of which one doubts strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound from the heart, and sew it up entirely without the cartilage; then administer remedies that promote flesh growth until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says one should not do this until the throat is completely choked, and the patient judged to be dead, and the failure of the windpipe.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	And then close the epiglottis so that the patient cannot choke, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is guarded from death; and because of this the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the maliciousness of the disease had passed, and it passes in three or four days. And then they commanded to sew up the wound and treat it, until it was healed; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw a maiden take a knife and stab herself in the throat, slicing open part of her windpipe; I was called to heal her, and found her as good as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound and found that blood had issued from it; I saw that it had not bled copiously or been directed outward other than through the throat, and the blood had escaped through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried and sewed up the wound, healing her until she recovered; the maiden was left hoarse, but returned to her usual state; thus I say that one should not fear cutting the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called a "gorge hernia", and it is a large abscess the color of yolk, often found in women; there are two types: natural and accidental; a natural hernia has no cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental hernia has two forms; one resembles a cyst, and the other is like an abscess coming from an artery; there is danger in it, and one should not attempt to force anything unless it is small, and one should probe and examine throughout the entrance: if you find it just like a cyst, and it cannot be pushed in at all, then cut into it as one cuts a cyst, and treat it as it should be treated, until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	of nuts
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many ways to treat dislocations, and I will describe all of their appearances; now I must explain the distinction between a displacement and an issue.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that an issue is a fever and heat which persists until the effusion has passed and the swelling is complete; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With a displacement there is no heat, fever, or pain, and it contains pus, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body; it begins like a boil and becomes swollen; and they are according to two appearances, either dry or moist, and in terms of color they are as I have described in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	When you come to the treatment of the nose, you should first examine and test it with all the instruments called "introductors," according to what its shape will allow in the following chapters.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the method of inquiring into abscesses is that you press on the moistest place that you find in the abscess, and repeatedly twist your fingers, until you feel that the pus has broken through the skin; then extract the pus, and be careful not to push any further.Et li maniere de la saignie est que tu prindras le sang ou la veine qui est plus proche de la piere et qui en va al corps, et li trunchons a la main et le piez; si fers le même por le bras et le col; et li trunchons soit selonc ses nombres.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If moisture runs out quickly, whatever color it is, treat it as I have said for other abscesses. And if after the incision no moisture comes out, know that it is fatty; therefore, cut it in a cross pattern and take it with tweezers, and lightly scrape each part and guard the wound where it lies so that you draw it clean with the needle. And if you cannot draw it clean, then draw it in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if it remains, the nose will return many times; and if a little remains, and the pain troubles you, then apply some corrosive powders to the wound, and bind it up with a hot abscess poultice, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed. And if the nostril is large, cut the two lips of the wound, and treat it with what heals ulcers.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the bleeding vein is contrary or elsewhere, then hurry and apply ground vitriol, and leave it for two or three days until the wound scabs over, and rest from the bleeding; then return to applying what was left off earlier.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here are the forms of the trocar, which come in three types: large, medium, and small. There are also three types of needle used for incising abscesses: one called an "albaret", another called a "breb", and there are also three types of these: large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the opening of the fistula. They are similar to the needles used for sewing sorcerers' wounds, made of brass, iron, or silver. The yellow ones are more effective, and those made of black lead are best for treating fistulous sores. They come in three sizes: large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the opening of the fistula.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of the knives are very similar, as you can see: large, medium, and small. There are also knives with two curves in three types; and knives with three curves, which come in three types as well; and knives with one curve only, which come in three types; and all of these are necessary for their respective purposes.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The heads of these instruments are sharp, and some cut only on one side, which is used to scorch the nose without cutting the vein or nerve; and with such instruments, bloodstains appear in many places so that the patient does not perceive when opening an abscess. There are three types: large, small, and medium, as you can see; and they are only used on fleshy parts like legs, arms, breasts, and similar areas; and sometimes a smaller instrument is made, resembling scorched fists, according to this form, with which blood is stanched.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and sometimes they put it into the place that heals by the opening of veins and arteries, and sometimes according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes men's breasts swell when they become corrupted, so that they look like women's breasts; and they remain ugly and swollen, and if one wants to cure them, one should bleed according to this form from the line .b. up to .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	then scorch the fat, and fill the wound with medicine encasing charcoal, then bring together the two lips of the wound with sutures, and treat it until it is healed; and if the mammary gland sags down, and becomes soft due to its size as happens to women, then make two slits above it, in the shape of similar slits; one holding onto the other at the end of both, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from line .b. to line .g.; then scorch the skin between the two lips, and remove the fat, and administer what we have said about sutures and powders, and what is necessary in the treatment, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not fully made, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to bleeding, then you should fill the wound with moist cotton saturated with a corrosive ointment; and leave it until it dissolves the remaining skin and fat, then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses on the scalp
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come under the scalp are types of hard scrofula, and there are some that contain pus.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who contain moisture must be cut according to this form, from line .b. to line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the abscess has been expelled, fill it with old cotton, and leave it until the next day; then remove all the cotton, and treat with a suitable ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess resembles scrofula, they should be treated as we have described for fissures of scrofula; and if a wound opens in the abscess, they should administer cautery as we have described above.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is large and the skin above is attached, this often results in abscesses, and similarly with a swollen vein and abscess; and one can identify it as due to the artery when the abscess is long and deep; and when you press it with your fingers, you feel tension; and when it is due to the vein, there are pus-filled bumps visible on the surface; and it is folly to cover this type of abscess, especially when located under the nails, on the fingers and toes, on the neck, or in other places, as it can be very dangerous.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, one must avoid cauterizing with iron and also avoid cautery on the head when it is due to an abscess on the artery; similarly, for an abscess caused by a swollen vein, one should make an incision along the vein from above the skin down to the artery, then pierce the artery with a needle at two places, and tie it off with a double thread at each place, as I instructed you in the extraction of the temporal arteries; then pierce between the two ties with an instrument, so that the blood flows out, and release the abscess; next, apply a poultice of warm wine and oil, followed by tenting and ointments until it heals; if the abscess is due to a swollen vein, one should take some pus from the abscess onto their hand, then pierce the vein with a needle at the place held in the hand, and pass a double thread through it, tying it off at both ends; then, if there is any doubt that the thread will slip out, insert another needle through the thread at various places along the abscess, and tie off the thread in three or four places; then lance the abscess to release the pus, scrape away the superficial pus from the skin, and leave the thread tied; finally, apply a moistened cloth, followed by poultices and ointments until it heals.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Also, as an abscess comes in the artery and vein, there are abscesses of the nerves when they are hurt, or from too much work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens most often in the shoulders and the elbows and in all joints where there are connections, and it is a painful abscess, and its color resembles the color of the body, and it is in various states without pain; and when one presses on it firmly, the patient feels pain, and it is not deep within the body but beneath the skin; and it becomes mute from all sides, and does not go forward or backward, or downward or upward, and that which is in joints should not be covered by iron: otherwise there might be contraction; and for that which is on the head or on the forehead, make a poultice with spatanil.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, hold it with tweezers and cut off its root; and if it is large, pierce it with an awl, and scrape it out, then cut out the bone and stitch up the wound to heal it.
des grosses boces pendans	large boils hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	At times it occurs in the belly and nowhere else; it is a disease called "fungus" because of its resemblance to ears, with fine roots and large leaves. There are small ones and very large ones; I saw a man who had two on his belly that looked more like fungi than anything else, without any difference, and they were white, with thin roots, and split open, and moisture ran out of them.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I cut them open and found one weighing 18 ounces and the other 6 ounces; the treatment for this is to make an incision if the disease is moist, and the color of the joint is white and moist with thin roots; then cut it with a spatulum widely, and have the fire cautery ready.
