Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For often there is excessive bleeding when cutting into a vein, and if the blood flows, then hasten to cauterize it; and if you see that the disease fears and is frightened of the iron incision, take a well-prepared thread of flax, and tie the joint as we have said, and leave it for two days; then bind it tightly, and do not stop compressing the flaxen thread until he cuts out the joint, and through it without effort; and if the roots are large, then fear the incision because of the belly, but you can certainly cut in half, then cauterize so that it does not return; then cure the wound, and be careful not to cut into the skin which is of a foul color and poor sensation and milk-like appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an abscess with an ulcer, and I will come to the treatment of ulcers later.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the boil has burst
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the boil comes from cauterization of a wound or from a fissure in the syphilis, and it is on the abdomen and some of the bowels, as it happens in other routs, or from blood flowing from veins or arteries according to what is before, or from flatulence; and if it is from the rout of syphilis and from the outlet of the bowel, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and it opens from diverse outlets.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the exit of the intestine, then it is more varied; when pressed with the hands, it springs back, and then returns, and sometimes it is constricted, and enlarges greatly at the entrance of the bath and from great effort.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	If it is due to moisture, it is a minor issue and opens easily when you press it with your hand without any restriction; and if it is due to blood, the abscesses are large and hard, and they are fixed according to a certain quantity; and if it is due to flatulence, it is soft to the touch, and the procedure involves checking whether the appearance is due to blood from an artery or vein, or flatulence.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If you need to let the wound heal.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, regarding the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is in the intestine or bowels, then you must command the patient to tighten his stomach and be stretched out straight, then sign all around the belly; then command him to lie still between your hands, then go around the area that you have marked all around the spasm, then press down on half of the abscess above the great toenail; then tie it tightly all around with a strong thread or strong silk rope, and let the nail be cut off from the toe; then open up half of the abscess stretched over the string, and probe the intestine; if you find it caught in the string, cut it free from the stomach; and if you find the bowel, grab it at the toenail and cut away the excess; and if the artery or vein is causing problems, go around it gently and then return to your work and take two needles, put two strong threads through them, and pierce what you have made into a cross; then pull out the abscess in four places with the needles, and if you see anything, remove the needles and leave the wound open until it drains, and cut away the dead flesh by itself; once it becomes thin and drains, clean the wound as needed and close it up.
dou chancre	of cancer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have discussed the appearance of cancer, and how to treat it with medicine, and how to avoid using iron in its treatment; and we speak of cancers that develop in ulcers, and great care must be taken in their treatment. The ancients say that when a cancer is in a place where it can be easily reached, like those on the breast, or thigh, or similar places, then one must remove it entirely as soon as possible. But for large and old cancers, one should not attempt to treat them, because I have never known anyone to be cured of such; nor has anyone ever been cured before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the treatment for cancers that can be reached, as we have said, is to first purge the patient with black colewort, then let him bleed if he has a manifest repletion, and then treat the cancer itself. Then cut away all the hair around it, and remove the bone underneath without leaving anything behind; and let the blood flow out freely, and squeeze the area with your hand or something else to ensure that all the blood is gone. If bleeding from an artery or vein makes the incision difficult, cauterize it until the blood vessels are sealed off. Then treat the wound further until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsyThe following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have already described in the division the appearances of dropsy, and how the accumulation of fluid is caused, and the signs of each appearance, and the treatment by medicine, and that which is cured by iron; only this is to be noted: one must not use iron for these two appearances: namely, tympany and hydrops, for they are deadly; therefore when you treat this appearance of dropsy, called "tympany", with medicine, and the cure does not help, then consider if the patient is feeble, or has another illness besides dropsy, such as a fever and similar things; in that case one must not use iron, for there is danger. But if you see the patient is of strong constitution, and has no other illness but dropsy alone, and is not too young nor too old, then one should proceed thus: lift the patient upright on your hands, and the minister presses the abdomen by pushing the fluid to the lowest part of the feet, then take the spathumile spine according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And cut into two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	And cut into two parts, but do not make it too pointed so that it can enter the intestines when inserted, nor should it bleed; then examine if the hydropsy is pressing against the intestines: if it is due to a disease of the liver, then your incision should be on the left side of the groin three fingers wide; and if it is due to the spleen, then make the incision on the right side; and you must not allow the patient to lie on the incision so that the excess fluids do not flow towards the weak area; then pierce the skin with your instrument, and insert it, and leave your hand on the spathomile between the skin and the syphax as much as a fingernail or an inch in width; then pierce the syphax until the spathomile reaches the desired location, and this is where the water is located, then pull it out, and insert your instrument to drain the fluid:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is similar to a silver cane, and is made of bronze or light archute, and has in the lower part a small hole; and on one side are three holes, two on another side, and one on another; and the head is cut like a feather, and this is the shape of the incision that the scribes make the pen.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	at the top of this is the funnel, so that when the instrument comes to a boil, it descends immediately onto the instrument; then empty half or a third of it, for if you empty more than is needed in that hour, by chance the patient may die from the disruption of his spirit due to the weapon, or he may fall into a faint, or he may approach death; but empty according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the sick man signify, and his pulses; then withdraw the instrument and retain the water, which is now retained by the membrane that blocks the hole above the throat, about which I have spoken, that you pierce in this way; then reintroduce the instrument the next day if you see the patient can bear it, and withdraw a little water; do this every day, and beware of overdoing it until only a little water remains.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	If you doubt the illness, let him drink a lot of water, and use the bath or hot sand, and through much sweating, and in the sun; and if he turns yellow from drinking, then treat with drugs that dry up, until he is cured; and cauterize over the stomach and liver and spleen after extracting the water, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	the swelling of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Sometimes children are born without a foreskin, or with a small foreskin, or it is not in its proper place.

puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close. Those who do not have an opening in their place are constipated, for some are born with the opening at the head of the penis, which prevents them from urinating until they lift their penis upwards; and they cannot ejaculate because the material cannot reach the outside, and this is a serious illness.

And the manner of the operation is that the patient lies on his back, then the head of the penis and the glans are pulled out to the size of a feather, so that the foreskin tears in the middle, as it should be; and you must guard against bleeding which often occurs, and if it does, stop the blood with something that stops blood, and cure the wound until it heals.
des pustules de la verge	of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez. The cauteries have two uses together: that is, for bleeding and for corruption; and if the glans of the penis is swollen and drawn in, then you must put a tube through the penis and let the patient urinate through it; and when the skin is raw at the tip of the penis which happens to those who have not been circumcised, or because of a wound or an abscess, then you must certainly scrape off the skin with an instrument, as far as the glans, and loosen and free the glans of the penis entirely; and if it is a serious thing to discuss this, then you should scrape it with a spatulum made from a little at the tip of the penis and through the foreskin; then draw it gently between two, and put a thin damp linen cloth in cold water over it so that it does not become raw again.
de la circoncision	on circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a natural process like other wounds; nevertheless, when we perform this act intentionally, especially on children, it is necessary to do it properly and gently for their safety.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of the circumcision of their children, for they did not use it in their law, and we have nothing on this subject except what we have acquired through experimentation.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen the greatest part of masters and surgeons who made circumcision all around the foreskin, and in many places, and on every new-born; then the hyleus would coagulate because there are two membranes, and sometimes one above would coagulate and the other below would remain.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Now they cover it again and the pain is doubled; and in the cleaning of the foreskin, which is not completely healed at the tip of the member; and in the cleaning of the fingernail, sometimes the nail escapes the fire, and the wound runs, and many times they are born with no need for cleaning, and I have seen this.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the cleaning made on the foreskin there is always the danger of cutting too much from above and below. I have found through experience that this is the case with all cuts.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Because when you press your hand, you cut evenly in I all forces; but the thread should be well wrapped around the skin; and the way of the first work is that you make the child think, if he understands, that you are only tying the thread around the pole, and then let him pull it in all the ways he can; then let him stand between your hands straight, and support the forces between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see them, or any of the instruments; then put your hand to the pole and breathe on the heart, and draw it up so that the head of the pole is in; then purify it well from the dirt that has gathered there, then tie the place marked with a double thread, then tie it under I to the other line; and hold it by the second tie with the index finger and thumb, and pinch between the two lines, then lift the heart quickly and draw the head of the pole; then let the blood run little by little, for that is the wound; and put powder on top of the powder, the drape glued with a cooked egg tempered with rose water, confit with good and fresh rose oil, and leave it until the next day, and cure it with another cure until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forces for cleansing is as follows: the two heads should be tense and pointed, and the heads should be as large as the palm equally:
