Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the afterbirth is retained during childbirth, you should instruct the patient to hold in her breath and then make her sneeze with a scent, and pinch her hands to her mouth and nose; and if she excretes through this, all is well.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, he takes a pot and makes an opening in the lid, and puts herbs that can open the mouth of the wound, such as wormwood, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia, and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, are cooked in water over fire; then he puts a tube into the pot, and the other end into the mouth of the wound, and blocks it so that the vapors go into the wound; then he makes him sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	Then let the pus drain freely.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this treatment and is not discharged, as it should be, then command the midwife to moisten her left hand with oil of ass's milk or with the mucilage of alder bark, and then put it into the womb, and seek out the placenta; and when she has found it, she should grasp it and extend it little by little straight down, so that the wound is not stretched on extraction; but it must be moved gently to the right and left, and then pulled out; it will come out and be discharged.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the disease is narrow, we have spoken of the cure for sneezing and the fumigation of herbs; but if it is not cured by all that we have said, be sure not to play with the bowels; but it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the disease, you tie it to the thigh of the woman, then cleanse it with ointment of four-fold medication; she will then evacuate and recover, but nevertheless, when she evacuates, a bad odor comes to the stomach and head, and damages the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore one should use suitable fumigations: some of the ancients have tried fumigation with watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The instrument used to fumigate the woman for retained placenta and afterbirth is as follows:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	It is like glass in appearance, and one puts the thin end into the body, and the broad end above the fire; and the fumigation is above the coals, and the stain until it is wasted away, and another begins again.
de percier lou fondement	of piercing the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have their anus pierced, but the rectum is closed with a thin membrane: therefore it is necessary for the midwife to pierce that membrane with her finger, and not with an instrument, and to keep the membrane from being torn; then she should put moist linen in wine and oil, and cure it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will heal, then place a wooden plug in the hole, and leave it for several days, and remove it when the child wants to go inside.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes the healing of a wound or abscess comes suddenly; so it must be covered suddenly: then it should be dressed, as we have said, with a plug of wood.
de la fistule dou fondement	from the fistula in the anus
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from under the anus are nodular, and grow larger than those that come from within the anus, or in the space between the two parts, whether there is one fistula or several; and when this nodulation is old, it opens, and usually emits white moisture or thin pus, and sometimes these fistulas are suppurating. They are perceived by the patient either in egestion or flatulence when the patient makes an egestaion, and occasionally a break occurs in one of them.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that pierce up to the bladder, and up to halfway down the penis; and they reach up to the joint of the thigh, and up to the head of the cow.Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And so one knows whether the fistula at the anus is suppurating or not; and it is known when you press your finger into the anus, and push a thin needle made of iron or steel into the fistula when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is twisting, one pushes in a thin tent of lead, or horsehair, as far as you can feel the tent or hair with your finger; and if you do not feel it, and no egestion or flatulence occurs, as we have said, then you know that it has not pierced through; so be quick about curing it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula has pierced to the bladder or the passage of urine, then the urine flows out and cannot be stopped by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is perforated up to the joint of the thigh, then the vein will also be affected up to that spot; if there is tortuosity and pain throughout, then it has become bow-legged, and ointments are of no use either immediately or after some time; in these persisting fistulas, there is no cure other than labor and the vanity of foolish people who interfere.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In one that is not perforated and is not old, there is hope of recovery through cauterization with iron, as I have experienced; the patient should lie on his back, and the physician should hold his legs up to his thighs, tilting his thighs toward his belly; then a tent made of bronze or lead should be inserted if there is tortuosity, until you know where the vein is.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it in the buttock, then you should insert your index finger if the vein is not perforated; and if you feel something between your finger and the flesh, then you know that it is perforated and cannot be cured by this method.Li tentures de ceste fistre sont perciez a la jointure des cuixes, et a l’estreme fin del tenture, li tendens se part en deux parties: une descende ad la fistre, et l’autre mont ad leu.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One can still heal some of them, but it happens rarely; and the help one gives, one burns the cautery subtly according to the width of the fistula, as has been said before; and fill it all with hot water in the fistula, so that it reaches the fundament; and do this two or three times, until you know that the false flesh is burned, which looks like a bird's feather; and then cure it with wet bandages of lamb's wool, until this flesh comes out, then cure it with ointment to join and heal.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is healed in this way, that is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If it cannot be healed in any other way; and if the tent goes inside and does not pierce to the anus which is at the fundament, and there is a thick covering of false flesh or syphac between your finger and the tent, and you see the fistula below this covering towards the bottom; then cut off the beginning of the fistula, and fill it up in front of the tent, and then burn with the cautery afterwards, so that it reaches the top of the tent; and the tent will be released and fall out; then scrape away this false flesh which looks like a bird's feather, and nothing will remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the pus runs, and cuts between your finger and the wound, then cauterize it with fire or with medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For fire cautery brings together two things: namely, the scorching of the flesh and the zastoning of blood and the drying up of moisture; then the treatment of moist tents with tallow or ground-up substances until the bowels gush out and the charred flesh emerges from the bowels; then treat the wound with quick-drying ointments on hard charcoal, and these are dry remedies.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes all the way from the anus, and is separated from the body, put your finger into it and probe it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent and within it is pus or flesh or charcoal, and it is ready to pierce through, then have strong hope and expectation through one of three treatments: either cauterize it as we have said, or cut it all the way down to the bottom; or if you can, place tents in there and treat it as before; do not go too deep, lest you pierce the lining that holds up the bottom, and let the discharge come out through the passageway; then treat it as before; perhaps it will be healed. Or remove that covering and cleanse it after cutting away from the bottom, either with tents or another pointed instrument; then dry up that diseased flesh in the wound, and keep the fistula from the part above the bottom: thus the ailment will be easier to bear.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes a fistula is formed in this way; and when you pierce the skin over the fistula, it is on the side of the fundament near the skin above, then take a needle pierced at the top in this shape:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And he ties .a. twisted thread in ii, and ties the thread all the way into the fistula until it reaches the root.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it pierces through the margin of the fundament inside, then pull out the thread from that opening so that you pierce your finger in the fundament; and pull on the thread's end, and bring the two heads together, and squeeze them together, and let it be for a day or two; and sometimes they squeeze it until the threads pick up the bits between them, and they cure the wound until it is sewn up and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not drain, then have it drained in every way you can, if it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not advisable to bandage the wound so tightly and then treat it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The shape of the spiny spatulum that is used to pierce a fistula is very sharp on one side, and not on the other; because it does not pick up what it should not, as you can see here:
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are of two types: either they are inside the anus, like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and some discharge blood, and there may be one or more of them, and they are outside the anus and at the top of the anus; but those that are outside have little moisture, and sometimes a little yellow water or a little blood, and they are the color of the body. The treatment for those who have them inside the anus is to command the patient to strain while going to the toilet until the hemorrhoids come out and the threads appear; then you hurry and grab it with tweezers, or hold it with your fingernail, then cut it at its root; and if the tweezers cannot hold it because of moisture, they grab it with a piece of cloth, or cotton, or a piece of chamois leather; and pull it out with their fingers, then cut it, and put some hot powder on top that is in the place of cauterization; or you can cauterize them as mentioned in the chapter on cauterization, then treat other hemorrhoids until it is healed; and if the anus cannot come out, then cleanse the patient with a sharp and harsh enema to wash away what is inside the anus so that it can come out clearly; when the patient strains, and if the hemorrhoid comes out of the anus, then the cure is easy; and you grab it with your fingernail or tweezers, cut it, then treat it as we have said until it is healed and fears incision with iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then you should administer the stitch in this way: take a twisted thread, and put it through a needle, then pull the thread from above, and pierce the needle from the other side; turn both ends of the thread underneath the needle, and let it be loose; then tighten the thread, tie it, pull out the needle, and do likewise for all others, and leave one to absorb the excess blood; then put a moistened cloth in rose oil or cerate over the wound, and command the patient to rest; then let him remain until he feels better, and when he is healed, treat him with ointment and other remedies.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	from dryness of the vagina or anus
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is dryness of the bowels in the intestines, and through constriction of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then you should cut off the skin at the tip of a spatulum or your nail, so that it does not retain moisture; then treat it until it scabs over as it should; and if it cannot scab, then repeat the scraping more forcefully than before, until it heals a great deal, and is scraped; then treat it until it is healed.
dou fremit	where it trembles
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Ant is a small appearance formed under the body, and goes very deep; and sometimes the cold freezes it, and one feels it as if dead from trembling, and it comes throughout the body, and more in the hands than anywhere else.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a cane of an goose feather, or a strong vulture feather, and place this cane on the trembling, until the purple circle trembles all around; then turn your hand over the entire cane as you touch all around the trembling, and push it deeply, and pull out the trembling by its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see fit to make this instrument of a feather of iron or steel according to this shape, and have it finely polished beneath and drawn above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not pierce it, so that it can be held in the hand and pressed firmly. And if you see fit to cauterize the vein, as described earlier in this chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the enema
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes an enema is made of silver or bronze, or melted copper or brass; and sometimes these instruments are small and large, depending on who they are administered to.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those that are administered to children and the weak and painful are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the enema, whether small or large, is inserted widely into the stomach, according to this method:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and has a decrease where the belly is tied, as you see, and the anus is pierced inside; and it has two holes on one side, and one on the other; and the belly is where one puts the medicines in a beast's bladder or parchment, and it is pierced all around with small holes, and there is one inch of space between each hole, then tie in these holes a strong thread of twisted thread in an X or around, and assemble the belly as if it were a goat; and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument in front with a strong thread, then colonoscopy; and this is the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	Let the medicine be neither too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head with oil or egg white, or similar, then insert it gently; then the minister should squeeze his two hands together until he is completely empty, then remove the enema, and let the patient lie on his side, and if the medicine wants to come out, let him defecate as much as he can; and if he sleeps for a night afterwards, that is even better.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you syringe him for a disorder of the stomach, and the medicine rushes out, then he should do it again until he is cured.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are in the anus or rectum, then the enema should be as thin as for a child; and this is how to make a thin enema that tightens the skin:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already discussed in the division of the treatment of wounds; now we will discuss the treatments by hand and medicine, according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and according to what makes them.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by the impact of a stone, or by sword and knife, or lance, staff, or arrow, or similar; or they may be made according to the places in the body, such as a wound that bleeds from the neck, head, foot, belly, liver, and similar members; and I will tell you how to cure each wound, and I will begin with simple wounds of the head, because their memory will come in their chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, one must be careful if it is due to a stone or similar object, and the skin is still intact but the wound is large, and you suspect a hot abscess: then have him bleed from the cephalic vein immediately if there is little blood coming from the wound, and let the bleeding be in the opposite direction of the injured part; and let the patient avoid fullness from wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to bleed, then let his food be diminished, and do not drink wine or eat meat; and put on the wound, if hot abscesses come, cotton moistened only in rose oil, or in stiptic wine; and if there is no hot abscess, then put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it has not been moved by air, a powder that I will describe shortly; and if it has been moved by arson, then put on some ointments until it heals.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like that of a sword, and the lips cannot be brought together with tenting, then bring them together by suturing, as I will describe for abdominal wounds.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to the bone, and it can be covered by only a little flesh, then close it with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat coarse foods, such as testicles and cooked wheat, as well as meat, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find pus in the skin, and it does not reach the bone, then scrape away all the pus, and wash it out, and then cure the wound; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which bleeds profusely, and cannot be staunched by medicine, then tie it off with a thread; and if that does not help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the cure is easy; you must apply this powder that will heal as soon as it has burned.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the method for the powder is as follows: take one part incense; two parts dragon's blood; three parts quicklime, and mix the powder finely, and apply it to the wound, and hold it firmly in place until it dries well and joins back together with its own blood; and then bind it up well, and leave it untied, if it is not swollen; for one should not remove the medicine until the wound is healed.Et se li plaie n’ait grant paor, et il ne peut demorer tant qu’ele soit sanee, si covient il que tu tu le traites per la cauterizacions des grans, ou si cuit en la plaie os de mort, ou os de bete morte, ou os de bete vive, ou os de chietif homme; car ce fu fait a Romme et en altre païs.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one does this with chalk alone, when one doesn't have incense or dragon's blood, but that the wound is moved by the fire.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the burn has moved the wound, stay in the same place, but do not put any powder on it; rather, apply some digestive ointments, or barley flour made from water and honey, until it becomes soft; then heal with other healing remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if a fracture comes with the wound and it is small, I will draw it out with subtle pincers; and I will tell you about fractures of the head later.
de la plaie dou col	about the wound on the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound is on the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is a nerve, do not treat it at all, and do not apply anything constricting, because it harms the nerves and makes them withdraw; and do not put anything cold on the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member; but let the medicine be warm, as in the case of a wash made from water and honey, and cooked with rosemary oil, and also washed in warm water, and other stones according to this method, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, cut and bind it, then heal it.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wound is deep and it is swollen and full of pus, then pierce it or a lower place; and if the artery is cut and bleeding ensues, then ligature and cauterize as needed; and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the windpipe, and the food passage is blocked, by which the meat goes, then press the windpipe on the Adam's apple, and do not touch the throat but reset it according to its natural shape; and then compress it gently, and leave it for some days, then treat it with ointments that promote sloughing until it heals; and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then trepan it; and if there are bone fragments, then remove all those you can, and leave those you cannot reach until the wound granulates and the sinus drains; and if the wound is fresh, then apply powder to the powder I have described.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and it has a fistula, treat it as I described in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of a wound from a spear or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a blow from a lance or knife, and the wound is deep, then examine whether the wound bleeds at all: then you will know that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, then do not put the powder on it in the first hour, nor bind it for the bleeding which will cease by itself, and return to the body, and heal the patient; but apply an attractive ointment, and change it twice a day; and if you do not have an ointment, then place old cotton in the wound to absorb moisture, and let the patient sleep with his head on the wound for three days, or four, or more; then no spasms, nor tremors of the body, nor constrictions of the throat will come; and when you see good signs, then you will know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat it with poultices and other remedies until it heals; and if it cannot heal, and the wound remains open, then you know that there is a fistula; treat it accordingly as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision, and it is superficial, in the front or back, then treat it as one does for wounds in those areas; if it is large, close it with stitches; and if it is small, treat it with powder; and if it has penetrated deep into the bone, and broken off pieces, then clean the wound, and extract any foreign objects; and for other wounds in other parts of the body, follow the method we have described.
dou derrompement dou ventre	a hernia
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	There are great, medium, and small rupture wounds in the belly; from a large wound sometimes the intestines, or the nerves of the intestines, are exposed, causing an external injury; and stitching is more difficult, and sometimes a small wound is worse than a large one because one must stitch up the intestines more carefully, going from warm to cool; for the intestines swell as soon as they feel cold, and return more easily to their place when warmed gradually; thus a small wound is often better than a large one, for one can reset the intestines more gently to their proper place than with larger wounds. And know that there are four types of belly wounds: the two common stitches occur in belly wounds, and the stitches for other wounds on the body; and yet they are more suited to belly wounds, and I will describe each type:
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and something of the intestines has come out, and it is easy to put back, it can be done in two ways: either because of the smallness of the wound as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this way: moisten a sponge or a soft cloth in lukewarm water, or cook in squint-water and cyprus and spikenard, and rose the intestines until the swelling is removed; and sometimes this wine restringent is made, and it is poured solely to reduce the swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling leaving, moisten the intestines with water or old wine in which mallows have been cooked, for there is an allergy to the entrance of a little thing; and if it cannot enter, make a small hole in the wound with the instrument by which one cuts hemorrhoids; and the first cure is better than cutting, which no one should do without great need; and that instrument serves to split it: so cut inside without breaking it out, and see the form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines jump out, then put them back in according to their natural shape in their proper place, if you have the strength, because this is best.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	And when the wound is low in the belly, you should make the patient lie on his back, and put his legs higher than his head; and if it is under the belly, put the head and feet higher than the lower parts, and also if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts, then put the wounded part higher than the other; and thus you should arrange what I say for large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, use what is appropriate for you, then hold in your hand a piece of linen which covers the entire rupture with one hand, and bring together the lips; and that is the common way to sew, and is that you pierce an needle or more, according to the quantity of the breadth of the wound, then leave at the head of the wound I finger's space, and insert a needle where there is a good strong thread; and pierce the two sides of the skin with the two sides of the subcutaneous tissue, which is under the skin inside, so that you make it pierce that part, and bring together the two heads of the subcutaneous tissue all four together; then tie the thread around the needle from both sides, then bring together the two sides of the wound comfortably, and then leave one finger's space, and insert another needle; then tie the thread as you did for the first needle, and do not stop doing this according to what you need in needles, so that all the wound is restrained; and the needles should be medium, between thin and thick, because thin needles cut all the flesh, and very thick ones cannot enter well: therefore they should be medium; and you should not push the needles too far into the flesh and the skin, so that they cut and open the wound before it is sewn; and then tie the ends of the needles, so that they do not hurt the patient when sleeping, and put tents or bands on the ends of the needles to hold them in place, and leave them until the wound is healed; and this method of sewing with needles is most suitable for small wounds, because it only requires one needle or two. The second sewing is common, and is that you bring together the two sides of the skin and the two sides of the subcutaneous tissue together on a needle where there is a strong medium thread; and when you have pierced these sides all four together, then bring the needle back to the part where you started, in the manner that one sews clothes; and put a finger's space between each stitch, the thickness of a thumb; this sewing heals the person, and I sewed a wound that a man had on his belly, which was cut by a knife, and the wound was more than a palm wide, and the intestines were exposed two palms wide, and the wound was in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned his intestines after they had been outside for 24 hours, and the wound was sewn up for 15 days, and I treated him, and he recovered.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And they looked at him and judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I didn't treat him with ointment because I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicine; and I placed old cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until he recovered.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper methods of suturing: take the needle and pierce it through the skin from the outside until it reaches the inside; then, once it has pierced through to the inside, pull the thread through so that it exits on the other side of the wound. The understanding of this method of suturing is such that you sew just like a tailor sews a piece of cloth, and you leave the thread hanging on one side, then grab it from the other, until the entire wound is sewn shut.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of sewing, which Galen describes correctly, is like how one joins two pieces of cloth together naturally, by applying the tip of one thread to the other, as follows: insert a needle at the tip of the thread, and pierce only that spot, leaving the two ends of the thread; then turn the needle and pierce from the outside in, all the way through to the inside, going through both pieces of cloth at the tip of the thread; then pierce both sides of the cloth from the outside in, going through to the inside, at two other points on the thread that are on the opposite side; this is the correct method of sewing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen describes this, and some testify to it: one should sew the belly with two needles, with thread in both; then one pushes one needle from one side, and the other from the other, as those who sew rotten cloth; know that when the rupture is in the belly, the sewing is more difficult than in other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgments of the wound are such as the judgments of other wounds: and it is that when you find the fresh wound all its blood, so that the burn has moved, then put back the intestines, and the fabric; then put on the powder of charcoal, and if the burn has moved, then put on any ointment that is present, until the wound heals; and cut the threads, and sew the fac, and the mirach; then cure the wound as the others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicine, put it on immediately when it starts to heal, old cotton, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you don't need any other medicine in various positions when the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound makes community with the principal members, then you should moisten light linen in warm tempered oil, or in rose oil, and put it around the angles, and under the armpits; and if he feels pain or swelling in the bowels, and it happens many times, then enema with warm red wine, and likewise if the swelling comes just to the intestines; and pierce it inside, and know that when it is the large intestines, it is easier to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines, which are called "young", cannot heal when they are raw, and this is due to the thinness of the veins through which they run, and the subtlety of the whole body, and their proximity to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the muscle jumps out of the wound, then put it back as you would with the intestines, while it is fresh; and if it is old and has become green or black, then you should tie up the black area so that no blood flow comes from it, for there are veins and arteries there; then cut what is between the ligature, and hang the two ends down from the part below the wound to aid extraction when the muscle slips out, and the wound is open.
de la routure dou boueil	of the boiling route
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestines are pierced, and the wound is small, then one can heal it in some people, for I saw a man who was stabbed in the belly with a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became swollen and a fistula formed, and through it came digestion and flatulence; I applied a dressing according to what I could, and did not cease to treat it until he was healed and the wounds closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him sweating, I doubted that the patient had pain in his belly; but he had no pain, but remained in better condition, eating and drinking; and some experimenters said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it must be bound in such a way: take a thread from a great testicle, then assemble the lips of the wound, and when the thread has opened its mouth, put it on the two lips so that it strains his mouth shut; and then tie the head of the thread, and it will stay so that it cannot come undone, then put another thread after in the same way as before, until the wound is completely closed; and then cut the thread.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the wound is in the intestine and no harm comes to the patient, one can sew up the intestine with a fine thread cut from an animal's intestine in such a way: take the end of this intestine thread, which should be very thin, and tie it to a fine twisted thread, then thread the needle and sew up the wound, and bring the two ends together; and this method of sewing with threads is good only according to the way of faith and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the intestines, there is no healing other than by subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it wakes up, is universally called a "fistula", and especially when it is swollen and becomes bow-shaped.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula is according to the green knotted node, hard and white, where there is no pain, and is as swollen as the feather of a bird; sometimes it is clear and bowed, and sometimes thick; sometimes small, and sometimes large enough; and I have already spoken about this in the division of wounds, that any wound which is not healed, and there is no pus, happens only due to one of nine causes: namely, because of the deficiency of blood or flesh; or because of evil; or because there is hard matter within, and on the surface, that does not allow pus to form; or there is too much swelling; or the place is porous, and the matter is of poor quality; or the medicine is not good in its treatment; or because the corruption is a type of pestilence; or due to the nature of the region, digestion and healing are slow, and there is swelling; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, their signs, and the medical treatments in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now I must tell you about the treatment of a fistula that is done by hand.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	You should know that fistulas occur in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that come from large veins, and from arteries, and from nerves, or from the syphilis, or from the intestines, or from the bladder, or from any of the ribs, or from the spine of the back, or from any joint of the hands or feet; and they can also affect the primary organ itself, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are in this way are of great harm to health, and there is nothing but labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come to a point where I have said, and you trust its cure, and see it to be known, then take an iron or bronze tent, if the fistula is straight, so take it; and if the fistula is crooked, then seek with a slender tent of lead, for the lead bends according to the crookedness; and if the fistula has multiple openings and you cannot properly explore it by tents, then cleanse it through one of the openings by enema, for moisture passes from one opening to another, and cleanses it; then press it hard with your hand, so that you know if there is bone or nerve, and feel how deep it is, and ask the patient about the pain he feels when you press his hand, and where he feels it most; and when you truly know the location, whether it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein, or any of the places I have mentioned, then treat it as I have instructed, and remove any foulness and putrid matter that remains within; then cure it until it is healed. And if the fistula is very deep in a straight place, you should treat it as deeply as possible, then moisten tents with medicinal water, and insert them into the fistula up to its head, so that the medicine corrodes the excess matter at the bottom; then apply soothing ointments to promote healthy flesh, until it is healed; if it is not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said. And if any bone is damaged by the fistula, then treat it as I have instructed.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If the vein or nerve does not bother the limbs, as we have said, and if the bone is exposed and there is decay and blackness, then treat it with king's yellow until the decay is gone, then cure it with things that are soothing until it heals; and if it does not heal, and returns to how it was before, know that you have not gone deep enough: then expose and dig until you reach the bottom, and remove all the decay, then restore the joint; and if it heals, that is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the decay is too deep for you to reach; then there is no other remedy but to let nature take its course; and if there is a small corrupt bone, and you can pull it out with tweezers, then extract it with the appropriate instrument for this purpose, and if there are many bones, pull them all out, and do not leave any behind; and if the moisture causes a contrarity, and there is no doubt or fear, then cut and dry, and apply soothing substances, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, then place something over the wound to promote suppuration, and let it fester around the bones, and then the bones will come loose more easily; and if it is a large bone, such as the leg or thigh, then cut away only the rotten part until all the blackness is gone, and then heal the wound; and if much of the bone is腐敗 and it reaches down to the marrow of the bone, then it must be scraped and covered over completely down to the corruption, and then it should be treated until it heals. And I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you can take example and help from this in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	He was a young man of about 30 years who had pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body, so that the matter came to his leg and it became swollen with a large abscess, and there was no reason to drain it; but the doctors, through their folly, did so much work on it that the abscess burst, and much matter flowed out, and it became a fistula, and many openings appeared all over his body from which matter and blood flowed; and many doctors treated him for two years, and there was no wise surgeon in the art of the hand, so I was called to him, and I saw his leg and the remedies with which he was being treated, and what flowed from the openings into a great wound; and the young man's body became red, and had a yellow color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I set up a tent in one of the holes, and then searched all the holes, and found that one came against another from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I hurried, therefore, and probed one of the holes until I uncovered a part of the bone, and found it corrupted and pierced, and the corruption extended to the bone within; I cleansed what appeared to me of the corrupted bone, and believed that there was no other corruption except that which I removed; and then I began to heal the wound with dry medicines for a long time, but could not close it; so I began again, and uncovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continued in the bone, and cleansed it, and then removed it, and labored to close the place; but I could not, until I probed around a palm of the bone, and drew it out entirely, then healed it with medicines; and it was healed and closed quickly, and there was no need to repeat the operation except for the weakness of the patient who could not endure, and for the fear of death that I had of him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	Because of the bloodletting, he often bled, but he was completely healed, and in place of the bone, a hard lump grew, and he had a good disposition and did not have any harm or contrary effects in any way, neither when lying down nor when getting up.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken anywhere in the body, one should treat it in this way: take a thread, and tie it to the head of the open bone, and instruct someone to pull it upward; and place another piece of linen larger than the first thread, and tie it over the lump that is above the bone, and draw the lump downward so that you draw out the corrupted flesh underneath, and uncover the flesh above where you see fit, so that the thread does not cut into the flesh; and place a hot iron or a board underneath the bone to cover the corrupted flesh; and one must keep tying it as far as one can see and feel the corruption, and tie it again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is broken and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, then uncover all of the flesh; then place a fire underneath, and then connect the two parts of the corruption, and pierce through to the length of the corruption, as we have said; and if the corruption is at the joint, then cut the corrupted joint, and join the bone on the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of both joints, then there is no other way to treat it than to cut; and if the corruption is in the palm of the hand or the sole of the foot, this is a very difficult thing, but nonetheless you must investigate the corrosion, how it presents itself; and cleanse it in every way that you can, but so that the vein or nerve do not harm you; and know that there are many tools for cutting these bones, according to the arrangement of the bones, and their appearance, thickness, subtlety, size, and smallness, and their hardness; and therefore one must prepare a tool for each appearance of work; and know that the work will show you the tool which you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of illnesses; then choose the tool which you need according to what is appropriate.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The heads can be injured either from within or from without; and when you have treated this injury with remedies but they do not help, then you must cover the affected limb up to where the injury is located, so that the patient escapes death by the greater evil, which is the defect in the limb; and the sign is that the limb becomes black, as if burnt by fire, and then the blackness appears, after which the injury spreads from limb to limb, affecting the whole body; so be quick to cover it, and if the cause is the sting of some venomous creature like a sea scorpion or adder or similar, and the injury is on the head, then cover it and do not give it space to reach the hand.
