Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it reaches the hand, then cover it at the joint so that the injury does not reach the arm; and if it reaches the arm, then cover it at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is fatal, and there is no remedy beyond the measure of its strength; and so you do with an injury to the foot: if it reaches the first joint, then cover it after the other joint; and if it reaches the foot, then cover the whole foot; and if it rises into the leg, then cover at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no remedy except to tie the limb with a bandage, and extend one of the bandages downward and another bandage upward, and you separate the flesh between the two bandages with a spatula as wide as a penny, so that the bone is uncovered; then cover and bind it, and place a linen cloth on each side so that the binding does not touch the healthy part, and does not cause the patient any further injury or abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if there is bleeding when you operate, cauterize the area firmly, or apply some restraining powders; then return to your treatment until it is complete, then tie the injured limb with a suitable ligature, and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man in his sleep: he had a discoloration that looked like a burn, and this corrosion first appeared on his big toe, spreading throughout his foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, he covered his foot, and it healed; and a long time after, the corrosion reappeared on his finger, and he came to me, and I applied some reflective remedies after cleansing the body, but he could not stop the corrosions; and he wanted me to cut off his hand, but I did not want to, as I had no hope of stopping the matter; and I also feared that if I cut off his hand, he would die, for the man's vitality was weak; and he despaired completely, returned to his land, covered his hand, and it healed; and I have only told this story so that others may learn from it if they need to.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	At times an abscess forms in a fleshy area, and remains so long that it causes a great gathering of pus; then it ruptures and pierces, and the pus flows out, leaving the place hollow like a vessel; and the skin above is as thin as a piece of cloth, and does not heal to the bone or nerve; such a disease is called a 'sore', and not a 'fistula'; but if it becomes so extended that it reaches the bone deeply, then it is called a 'fistula'; and the skin is such that you can grasp it all around, and especially when it is thin, like a piece of cloth; and it does not heal over by itself.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you have reason to believe that the skin is healing and the corruption is not deep, but the flesh is thick, then treat it with a clyster thus: look to see if the breast is swollen and the pus has an odorous smell, then clyster with Egyptian medicine which is made in this way: take equal parts of asafoeida, oil and litarge, and put them into a vessel over fire until the medicine turns red and as thick as honey; then take some according to your need, dissolve it in water and honey, and clyster the breast and press out the pus; leave the medicine in for two hours, then expel it by squeezing; do this several times until the breast is cleansed and the sore healed; sometimes you may use clysters of ash water when Egyptian medicine is not available: take vinegar ashes of vine wood, pour water over them, let it stand and strain out the liquid, and use to clyster the breast until you see that it is cleansed; if the patient cannot bear the Egyptian medicine or ash water, then use a clyster of water and honey with a little litarge ground in it; or clyster with honey and wine where the honey has the property of cleansing and washing, and the wine makes the sore dry; and when you have done this and seen that the breast is cleansed, then clyster with something that causes flesh to grow in it, and take diaphanous plaster, mix it with rose oil and wine, or use some other medicine or ointment of which I have spoken concerning their properties in the section on ointments; if the opening of the breast is small so that the clyster cannnot enter, then enlarge it a little with iron, and put in a tent of Egyptian ointment, or basilicon ointment, as far as it can reach; if the wound is too large, cut away only enough to allow entry of the clyster where the opening that drains pus is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	Because when the bowels are in perfect health, one should not leave excrement inside; and if you cannot cover the breast underneath as you wish, then arrange things so that the bowels move to the lowest place they can, for when the bowels are healthy, one should not leave excrement inside, and if you cannot cover the breast underneath as you wish, then arrange things in such a way that the bowels move slightly downward, and do not leave anything of the bowels; take consolidating medicines to put on the wound, and place them on the linen cloth that covers the entire wound; then cover the most forceful spot of the breast where it is widest compared to the first one, then apply an ointment on the other cloth according to the quantity of the wound, and place it over the wound to ease the bowels, but do not remove the large cloth for several days; and that which is placed over the wound, remove often to remove the bowels, and know what comes out of the bowels, whether it is venom or pus or enough, or digested, or undigested; take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has extended in such a way and you see the nature that rises on the wound, then know that the breast is healing, and approach the sana. Then loosen it in the morning, or midday, and when you loosen the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast milk flows badly after many days, know that the breast does not heal.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons spread after a long time, do not despair of health, for health is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are people whose wounds fester for a long time with putrefying flesh, and others who have the opposite condition; and if indigested food sits in the stomach for many days, know that the stomach is not healing; and if the stomach takes a long time to heal and is distant, then apply dry medicines that are moist in substance but dry in virtue, such as diaphanous ointment, for it contains a large amount of vitriole, and it is the best medicine; take diaphanous ointment and mix it with rose oil, and rose water made from old wine, equal in substance; then cook it and use it; and if you do not have diaphanous ointment available, you can use honey cooked with oil, and when you do not have that, take myrrh, aloe, and incense, grind them into a powder over the honey while it is on the fire; then apply this to a cloth and place it on the stomach, and sometimes an aristology is administered for a long time, as well as roots of celestial lilies, which are like flour made from fava beans and centaury; and use simples or compositions: grind them into a powder and mix with the honey I mentioned, then use it; and if the fistula takes a long time to heal and is not healed by this treatment, then know that the corruption has reached the bone, or to the hard tissues, or to the soft tissues; and then follow the fistula treatment as we have described earlier.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess that arises underneath the nail of the finger or toe, or sometimes in other places; and when it becomes infected, and no attention is paid to it, then a hard abscess forms, and it runs and seeps beneath the nail, all the way to the root of the nail, and sometimes even further; and it eats away at the bone, causing a foul-smelling pain, and the area around the joint becomes swollen, and the color is discolored.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have described in the section on treatment, and the treatment does not help, then you must cut away all the excess tissue that is remaining under the nail, and then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cautery is a great help if the bone is healthy and the nail is also healthy; and if the nail is pressing on the flesh, and starting to grow over it, then you must put a piece of cloth under the nail so that it does not touch the flesh, and tie it up above, and carefully cut away the dead flesh, and apply burning and corrosive medicines to remove all of it; then treat the wound with ointments until it heals.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	If the corrosion is in the bone, cut it out and pull it out, for as long as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal; and if you see the tooth decay, cut it out at the gum, as has been said before, then cure it until it is healed; and if it is infected and pus-filled, causing great pain, you must treat it first; then cut the nail of the finger with an angle cut from above, and be careful that the cut does not reach the flesh under the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if this happens, place something to soothe it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the deafness of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two joints that grow on the hands of some men by chance are all fleshy, and sometimes there is bone, and sometimes a nail, and sometimes they grow at the root of the joint, or in one of our fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Those born with a hernia in the navel do not move, but those born with one at the joint of the neck may move; the size of the one from the fleshy part is slight and should be cut at its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint is difficult to cure; if you hold it tightly, it will stop bleeding.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For one born with a hernia in the rear navel, you must first cut around the flesh circularly to the bone, then cut the bone with an appropriate thread for that, then cure it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The joints that come together come from birth, or from the joining of a wound, or from arson, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	Then you must cut that suture so that the intestines return to their natural shape; then place between two wet tents or cloths moistened in rose oil, so that they do not adhere; or between two pieces of thin plank, until the skin is sutured, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If swelling comes to either of his hands with the palm, then cut that wound as it should be.
des vils	the poor
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Veins are large tubes wrapped in full of melancholy superfluities, which come in many parts of the body; and they occur more in legs of those who walk and work and carry loads, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should administer to him a purgative, and then the basilicum herb.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment with fire is in two ways: one is that you cut the skin and draw out the black blood; the other way is that you open a vein and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The incision is done this way: first heat the leg with very hot water until the large veins are dilated, then stretch the leg from above the thigh to below the knee; then cut the skin in one place, or two or three, with a wide incision, then open and draw out the black blood to your hand, from one end to the other, until as much blood comes out as the patient can tolerate; then ligate it, and command that he eat meat with garlic mixed with black pepper; and start the evacuation and bleeding again when the incisions are healed, and rest.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The treatment of dislocation is as follows: raise the leg of the patient, if there is a lot of hair, then put it in the bath, and heat the leg with hot water until it turns red and the veins swell; and if you do not have a bath, then heat it over the fire, and then press on the vein from the top to the knee, or in the part below the ankle; then open the skin at the nail, and scorch the vein on each side, until it appears when one feels it; and one sees it red and black, and when it enters the skin it looks like a white cord; then pour water under it, so that it is lifted from the skin, and then press it gently at another nail; then press another incision, or more if you need to, then lift and press it at the toe, then draw and lift it up to the second incision; then pull it out from incision to incision, until it is all out, then press it; and if you cannot pull and lift it, then insert a very strong double thread with a needle, tie it and pull it, and pour water under the thread, and turn your hand from side to side, so that it comes out; and be careful not to cut it, because if it is cut, it cannot be pulled or lifted, and it brings harm to the patient; and when you have treated it all, then place moist wool soaked in wine and rose oil over the wound site; and dress it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the wound is contracted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must split it twistedly, but do not cut it; and treat it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron used to split a wound is curved, and does not cut into the vein; it is a broad curve, for if it were slender, it would cut the vein, but it should be large as we have said, and thus is its shape:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is twisted in the legs, in dry regions where no herbs or trees grow, and in land with no moisture; and it sometimes appears elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens from the growth of porridge-like substances that come under the skin, just as snakes and worms emerge within the body, twisting between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this wound are that a great inflammation comes in the leg, then the place changes, and the wound begins to come out forcibly, just like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the shoulder opens, you should wrap a piece of woolen cloth around it from 3 and a half to 4 inches, and tie it, and leave the cloth hanging on the leg, and every time it comes out, wrap it around the cloth again, and if it is too long, cut off some, and wrap around the rest, but do not cover the root while it is still coming out; because if you cover it, it will go back into the flesh, and cause an abscess and swelling in that place, and a serious illness; therefore this wound should be treated little by little until it is all healed; sometimes it is as much as 5 or 10 palm-lengths long, and once I had a patient whose wound was 10 palm-lengths long, and when you cover it, it makes a hole, and pierces right to the bottom, so that everything comes out; then the matter inside should be emptied, and soothing medicines applied to the place for a day or two, and then it is treated like an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes this vein bleeds profusely, especially when it opens at the joint of the foot or the leg, and a lot of pus comes out, and from which it rains; therefore treat it as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of worms that grow between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called "cattle disease" in our land because it often affects oxen, and it is a small worm that grows between skin and flesh, and travels throughout the body, going up and down, and is felt everywhere as it moves from one limb to another until it breaks the skin where it goes, and bursts out; and it is caused by the putrefaction of certain humors, just as worms, snakes, leeches, and roundworms grow in the belly; and there is fear of its malice, for when it travels through the body and goes up to the head, it may enter the eye and destroy it, and this often happens.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it being cured and drawn out, you cannot help but when he urinates: therefore you must tie the place above and below with a strong ligature tightly, then press on it from above and draw it out forcefully; and if the pus is deep in the flesh, and you do not draw it out, cauterize it with fire until it comes out; and the greatest harm that it does is that it runs into the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming near to the eye, tightly constrict under it the eyelid, then press on it from above and draw it out forcefully; and one must use the cleansing of the body with soluble medicines for the putrid humors, and a diet of warming foods to produce urine.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from flatulence
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called "vomiting" in our land, and it is a pain that occurs in some members, and then moves from member to member; and I saw what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and I uncovered her arm, and saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and a little later, I saw it rise up her shoulder as quickly as a worm, faster than anything, as bright as silver when it moves from one place to another; the pain left that spot, and settled in her shoulder, and then a little later spread throughout her body, until it reached her other arm; then she told me that she was spinning around her body, just as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly how she moved from limb to limb in this manner, for I had never seen this illness act in this way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Nevertheless, I have seen many whose pain moved from one place to another, but I did not see it in the woman; and I thought that it was because she had a dry body, and her veins were exposed, and so this windiness manifested itself constrainedly; and it did not appear that way according to this reason to those who are delicate, and have moist bodies and relaxed veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see to treat this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears to you as we have said, then press above and below gently, and then apply a compress until that forced wind is released; and cauterize the area; and if you do not see it yourself, then treat it with those who dislodge winds, such as foul pills, and serapin pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse according to their appearance and according to where they land on the body.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The varieties of them are that there are some with large points, and small, and curved, and straight; and some with two angles, and some with tongues, and some with pieces; and those which break in any limb fall according to two manners: either in a principal limb, such as brain, heart, liver, lung, spleen, intestine, bladder, and similar limbs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When she falls in any of these places on the body, and the sign of death that I will tell you about appears: then you should be careful about removing this arrow, because death comes afterward in many dispositions; and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not fully embedded, then pull it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain is when the arrow pierces the bone and hits the brain, it is when there is scotomata and confusion and trembling and red face, and inflammation and reddening of the tongue, and spasm and disturbed mind, and vomiting of phlegm; and perhaps there is discharge from the nose or ears; and perhaps they lose their speech and voice; and out of the wound comes white moisture that looks like pulp, and also as bruised flesh; and if this sign appears to you, then stop the treatment and pull out the arrow if it is not already out.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The signs of a seizure when it occurs in the heart are that it is close to the left breast, and feels as though it were pierced by a hard object, and is not visible; and sometimes the seizure is silent like the pulse, and emits black blood, and there is chilliness and cold sweat, and syncope: so you should know without doubt that death is near.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that never leaves the lung is that there is no pain from foam coming from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and breathes heavily and seeks the cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow hits the cover of the foot, it is between the small ribs; and it causes great pain and great discomfort and breathing difficulties; and all the limbs from the shoulders are affected.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow hits the stomach, by chance some indigestible meat may come out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow pierces the chest or belly, and no feces come out through the intestines, then there is no hope of a cure, nor of extracting the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrow pierces the bladder, and urine comes out and escapes, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face, neck, throat, shoulder, elbow, spine of the back, hip, thigh and legs, and similar limbs, are safe according to various dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you how to do this.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	A certain person had a seizure that fell into the jaw in the root of the nose; I treated it, and released it below the fat of the ear, and was cured without any trace.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And I treated a person with a seizure that fell into the fat of the eye below, under the eyelid, and the seizure was retracted, and only its tip could be seen from the nose; the seizure was as large as an arrowhead, but very thin without ears; the person was cured and no ill effects occurred.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And I took an arrow out of the throat of a Christian, and it was an Arabic arrow that went into his ears; I removed the barbs and extracted it, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I also took out an arrow from a man's home that had gone into his belly, and I thought he was going to die; but after thirty days passed, his condition did not change for the worse; so I cut into the arrow, inserted something into it, extracted it, and he had no bad outcome.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you see a person who has an arrow stuck in his back, and the wound is sewn up on top of it; as long as the arrow remains inside him, and his natural functions remain unchanged, and he experiences no harm in any of his natural processes, then:
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	You will see another man who has an arrow in his face, and the wound is sewn up; he remains like this without suffering great pain, and there are many other similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And I treated an arrow wound in the home of the prince the king, which had pierced his eye, and was slightly inclined to the right side; and the arrow was fully withdrawn after three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I applied a subtle cautery to it, and did not feel anything; but he felt a piercing pain beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the point of the arrow. I placed a soothing and digestive poultice on the site to prevent inflammation of the wound; and I saw the wound of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I applied the poultice again and again, and the wound healed quickly, but the man felt the arrow inside his eye for a long time; and he told me so.Apres ceu que li fu la saiette cheue, je alai a sa cure, et trovi le home en gran dolor et mult estroite de la plaie, si com me dist; et il m’otreit mult de l’ongle del doigt quare il se frotteit les euus.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied corrosive medicine to the wound for several days until it was open, and probed it, and felt the tip of the arrowhead which was embedded; then I inserted the medicine into the opening of the wound until the head of the arrow became clearly visible; and the wound healed completely within four months, and then I lanced it, and pulled with tweezers from both sides, but it would not come out; therefore I did not cease to apply subtle instruments and devices in various ways, until one day I was able to grasp it with well-made tweezers, according to the shape that will be described at the end of this chapter, and so I extracted it and healed the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And those who saw it judged that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored; therefore I restored it, and the wound was closed and the patient completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Now I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you may put your treatment on what I do not say, because books cannot encompass everything; but wise masters reason well about very few things, and about what they are present and lacking, they devise new work and new instruments, at the descent of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows grow in the members where they are stuck in two ways: either by the place where they enter or by another part; and that which goes out by the place where it enters is an arrow entering into fleshy parts, and sometimes goes out now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not go out now, then leave it as long as the flesh around it becomes rotten and the outlet is relieved; and also if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, then leave it for several days, and move it every day; and then it will come out, and if it does not, then pierce through to the very tip of the forest, so that the holes around it become enlarged, and then pull it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	If the arrow is lodged in the bone of the skull and pierces through to one of the brain's ventricles, and if any of the signs I have described manifest in the patient, then do not extract it; rather, let it remain until it becomes even with the surface after a few days. For if the arrow reaches the brain, this is certain death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is lodged only in the bone and does not reach the brain, and the patient survives for several days without any adverse signs, then attempt extraction.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very deep and cannot come out, then administer cauterizations around it as I have told you; then treat the area until it heals.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is lodged deep in the body and cannot be seen, then probe for it throughout the wound; and if you feel it, extract it with an appropriate instrument. And if, due to the depth of the wound and the penetration of the arrow, there is no bone, nerve, or vein in the way, then open the wound widely; and if there are ears or barbs on the arrowhead that are holding it in place, carefully remove the flesh around them from both sides as much as you can, then break or bend the ears so that you can extract the arrow. Be careful not to break the arrow while extracting it, lest you push it further in.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot in one go, then leave it until around the joint is swollen; then draw it out, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	If the bleeding persists in spite of your efforts to stop it, then follow what we have said about treating the wound in its own chapter; and be careful to avoid cutting into a nerve or opening a vein, and draw out the arrow as quickly, firmly, and gently as you can; and put the patient back into the position he was in when the arrow struck him, for that is the best way to help him. If you cannot do this, then at least put him into the position indicated by the wound.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	An arrow that comes from another direction, or where something can be seen or felt underneath the skin: cut into it with a knife until the clamp can grip it, and then pull it out; if it won't come out right away, try again later.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is caught in the bone, then rotate your hand swiftly as far as it will go into the bone and widen the opening, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	If it cannot be pulled out, then leave it and try again later; if part of the arrow is exposed, push it all the way in; if only the tip is showing, and you can see that there is some room to manipulate it, then slide the tip of your instrument into the wound so that the arrow tip enters the groove of your instrument; then pull it out, and if the arrow is stuck in the instrument, push the instrument all the way in to ease its extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	If the arrow has struck a vein, you must cut away all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can, and then treat the wound as it should be.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If the arrow hits the leg or foot or belly or bladder or side, and it is deep, and you can cut above it, do so; but be careful not to cut the vein or nerve, and then extract the arrow, and cut the wound open if necessary, and treat it until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the forceps used to treat arrow wounds resembles an owl's beak, and here is its shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many types: large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the arrowhead.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrowhead is like the feather on an arrow, to catch at the tip of the arrow, just as it is shaped.
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of tongs for gripping and probing is thus:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are 31 veins from which one can bleed, and in the head there are 16 of them: two that are behind the ears, called the "ear-veins"; and two arteries in the temples, visible; and two veins that are in the corners of the eyes, called "aspires"; and the vein that is in the forehead; and the vein that is at the root of the nose; and the two veins in the neck; and two veins that are above the lip, and these are the veins called "age-herbs"; and two veins below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	Veins are commonly used for healing in each arm: one is the cephalic vein, located on the left rib cage, and ordinary people call it "vein of the head"; the middle one is called the "fast", composed of the cephalic and basilic veins, and ordinary people call it the "vein of the heart"; the basilic vein is located on the right rib cage, and ordinary people call it the "vein of the belly", and it is above the cubital fossa, and it is the one used for healing, which clearly opens above the elbow.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the salvatelle is the vein between the auricular and annular veins, and there are two rains in it; and in the leg and foot, there are three veins: one is below the bend of the left rib cage, and the second sophene vein is at the ankle of the right rib cage; and the vein called  "nesse" is at the ankle of the other rib cage; and in the other leg, there are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The bleeding of the veins that are behind the ears is helped by old catarrhs and by emigration; and the qualities of the bleedings, as I have told you, and it is that you raise the head of the patient, and rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then press the patient's neck to a vise, so that the two veins appear behind the ears in two places depending on the head: grasp them with your thumb, and where you feel the pulse under your thumb, sign there; then take the lance, and insert it beneath the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand to all of the vein upstream, and pierce through both skin and vein well with your thumbnail, and make the blood come out; then press and ligate it, until it is healed; and I have already said about the incision and cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The bleeding of the two arteries that are in the temples, it helps to cure old migrain, and headache, and habitual ophthalmia, and ague in the eyes; and the quality of the bleeding is as I said: and it is that the patient turns his neck, so that the two veins appear clearly; and feel the pulse under your thumb, and then sign on; then raise the heart above the vein at the top of your index finger, and insert the lancet underneath, and raise the vein above, and cup it, as you have done in the other veins, and let the blood according to your need; then loosen the patient, and put your finger on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on it; and then bind it tightly, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken of their binding and their extraction, at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The bleeding of the vein in the forehead is as good as the bleeding of the cephalic vein for old facial diseases, and for мигрень, and for redness; and its qualities are such that the patient turns his neck until the vein appears; then take the instrument called "fosseur", of which this is the shape:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point upon the vein, and press up with your hand, or something else, and let the blood issue according to the quantity that you see; then release the patient's neck, and tie the vein until it is healed, and sometimes the operation is performed with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not advisable for the flames to be too small; and heal it crookedly, because the bone is close by, and accidentally break the flames when they are thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The bleeding of the two veins that are in the temples helps with eyes, and with тин, and with redness, and with an eyelash in the eye, and with facial diseases; and the qualities of their bleeding are such that the patient turns his neck by twisting some ligament, as before; then bleed him, and let the bleeding be through a small hole, with a wide flame, for there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are thin, they might break; then draw out the blood, as much as you need to, and then tie it up with a thread, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The bleeding of the vein in the nose is good for a cold, and a violent fever, and facial diseases, such as a migraine and redness that comes in the face, and especially when it is chronic; and the quality of the bleeding is such that the patient squeezes his nose, then pulls his ears to the left hand, and takes a long, thin flame, and inserts it into the lip in the space between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open well otherwise, and the blood will begin to flow now; and do not go too deep, and let the blood flow according to your need, then tie it off overnight, for it is quickly restored; and this is the shape of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The bleeding of the two sinuses helps with laryngitis, and the beginning of hoarseness, and many diseases, and pemphigus, and corroding sores, and herpes, and stomatitis; and the quality of the bleeding is such that the patient squeezes his neck from side to side, as we have said; and let the master stand above the head of the patient, and the patient sit on a chair, then bleed the vein a little widely at first, then draw the blood gently, or as much as is needed; then do the same in the other vein, then loosen the ligature, and gently squeeze both veins so that the patient does not choke; and let him be until the morning, so that the wound can heal.
de la sainie des leivres	of bleeding gums
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The bleeding of the veins of the lips helps with ulcers in the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and splitting of the lips, and toothache and gum pain.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the nature of bleeding is to have the patient sit facing you and to hold his head as I have said; then turn up the lip, and look at the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, which can be recognized because they are black and because there are thin black veins around them: press both of them, and if you cannot recognize them and you doubt which they are, press the largest vein on each side; and do the same with the two veins above and below, for it is the same procedure.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of bleeding under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The bleeding of the veins that are under the tongue is helped after the bleeding of the head, and it is in the constriction of the throat, and in diseases of the eye, and in diseases of the mouth; and the quality of the bleed is such that the patient lies between your hands facing the sun, and you loosen the tongue, and look underneath on each side for a black vein: therefore heal one and the other, and do not go too deep, because beneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the neck that are commonly bled are bled in two ways: either with a pointed mirtin [flame], wide or olive-shaped and very fine, called 'anesil'; they are wide or fine according to the width and constriction of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the steel needle is very important, and it should be as thick as a thumb:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the flat veins with a lot of visible thick blood, and those that contain thick and troubled blood; and this is the shape of the olive-shaped flame.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more pointed and sharp, and is used to lance delicate veins, where there is delicate yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The basilic vein, which is one of these veins, helps diseases that are beneath the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the belly; and the surgeon must cut it bleeding, and he must cauterize the artery that is underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he pierces the artery and bleeding ensues, it must be staunched as I have said; and the flame must not be gripped but snipped like a thread.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilic does not open clearly, you must stretch it and change to another; or you take some of it, or you cut the vein in its place in the arm: it opens clearly; and grip the flame gently, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you wish to know the place of the cut, you must stretch the arm, and touch the spot until you feel the pulse; then mark the spot on the inside, and then bind the arm, and cut the vein with the flame gently; and be careful not to pierce the artery when you see the spot puffed up, for that is the artery: avoid it therefore.Et li sainiez de la veine qu’est entre les deux mambres, et qui est la costez del col; si covient a l’usager que il saine saignement; et qu’il warse l’artere qui li est desoz, et qui est sus le poilz.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it rise up as high as a child's urine, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is arterial blood: therefore hasten, and put your finger on it for a long time, then take away your finger if it stops; bind the arm, and leave it thus, and do not move the patient; and let him be in fear, and do not move him until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not staunched and it flows, and you have no medicine at hand, then press upon the artery to open it, for that is where the blood retreats, and staunch the flow.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take a piece of ficus, and split it, and take one half and bind it on well until the next day; if the bleeding stops, that is good; if not, then treat it, as we have said, with powdery substances that stop bleeding; and stopping the bleeding is not harmful in many cases because of the small size of the wound, and because of the strength of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The bleeding of the vein in the middle [of the arm] is helped by causing blood to flow from the head above and the body below, because it is composed of basil and cephalium, as we have said; and the surgeon must be careful not to pierce too deeply, and if he does, and hits the nerve, and it swells and the bones are bruised, and perhaps cannot heal; and this nerve often opens, and if it doesn't in some men because of its subtlety, then you should treat it with a silencing instrument; and protect the nerve to the best of your ability.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, they will make it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The bleeding of the cephalium is helped by causing blood to flow from the head and helping the eyes; and it must be bled with a flame of olive oil or a flame of myrrh, for it is the safest of all veins, because it has no nerves or arteries beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Nevertheless, one must seek the lightest place and cause no grief if it fails the first time, then try again; perhaps the places will swell in some men if they fail the first time, but it causes no harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of bleeding depends on your thoughts.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you should know about bleeding is that it is not done until after maintaining health and preventing future illnesses; and bleeding should be performed in one of the three veins: the head, the arm, or the base of the palm; and bleeding should be performed at the beginning of Lent, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the signs of digestion are apparent; and bleeding should be performed on the first or third day, after two or three hours of the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	Bleeding that is administered for illnesses does not have a set time, but whenever there is a need during the day or night, in all hours and at all times; and one must not bleed children until they are 14 years old, nor women carrying after the fourth month until the seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should the very old who have passed 60 years be bled.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.
