And when someone wants to be bled, in whatever way it may be, one must cleanse the intestines with a gentle enema if he has retained much feces, so that the veins do not draw harmful, excess fluids from the intestines into the main limbs; one does not bleed those who are bloated from eating too much meat, or who are drunk, unless they have abstained for some time, nor the sickly and the weak; and one must not bleed after a colic attack, vomiting, diarrhea, and frequent intercourse with a woman, nor after excessive exertion, watching all night, or fasting, nor those whose strength has been depleted by an injury to their limbs or their body; then gently cleanse the humors through food, drink, and medicine if you have the skill; then enter the bath if nothing else will help to cleanse the blood, and be bled around the navel on the third day, as we have said; and guard against exertion, pain, and lust that day; and be calm and cheerful, and let the person being bled lie higher than the bleeder, and rub the arm two or three times, then gently tighten the ligature above the middle, for if it is too tight or too loose, it will not draw out the blood; then rub the area with your hands until the veins swell and you feel them; then moisten the bleeder's flame with a little old oil, then place the tip of his left-hand index finger over that vein below where he wants to bleed, so that the vein does not shrink away from the blade.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	Because there are veins that flow like cords to the armpit, and some that are filled with winds, so that when one puts it over the flame, it draws back from the flame and cannot open the vein, and thus one is of those; and if he opens the vein, the wound is too tight, therefore the surgeon must be skillful in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, that is good; if not, then try again a little lower on the same spot, or above, if the area is swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the arm is swollen, and the patient is frightened, leave it for a day or two, and do not bind the arm: perhaps hot abscesses will form; do not enter into the bath, then restart the bleeding if she pleases; and if the opening is small, let the blood flow gently and subtly through it, and you doubt that it does not flow as much blood as you want, then apply the flame directly to that small opening; and work gently, so that the arm is swollen; because this happens many times when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the place swollen, do not re-open the wound, but put a little lamp oil on it, for it lightens the body of blood, and in this place the oil is changed into fat; and thus administer lamp oil to each vein that you open, to stop the flow of blood; and the same thing happens to water and milk when one puts them on the wound; but subtly the blood and milk split when they are too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there is a large abscess that often occurs, especially when the opening of the vein is small, be quick and put a sponge soaked in warm water on the wound for an hour; and you should do this after the flow of blood from the vein has stopped, and if there remains blackness or green color at the site for several days, it will not harm him; and if you see anything, apply a remedy made from aloe or myrrh dissolved in water.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times there is an abscess and appearance of pus at the site of the basilic vein; therefore, place your hand on it, and if you feel the area soft to the touch upon compression with your hand, then that appearance is bad.Et si tu veis, met sus le leu esponge moillie et chaut, ou l’estraincture de la main, si ne tu veis aucune noiror ou verdor;
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore be sure not to put anything on it of what we have said, for by chance it might enter an artery; but let him make a dry plaster to harden the spot, then heal it with another healing, until it is cured.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw from each person blood according to the quantity of his virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if you see it thick, let it flow until it becomes thinner; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for one who is full and swollen, and needs bloodletting, that a larger wound is made, and the flames should be wide; and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and they should be bled little and often, and one should bleed them by cutting across, not piercing; and this bleeding method is safe from blood loss and nerve damage, and it is better than bleeding long or wide.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for one whose body needs bleeding, one should give them moist bread in pomegranate juice; if they are hot-tempered, then take blood three or four times. And if of a cold complexion, eat moist bread in muzed syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chicory, and well-scented syrup before bleeding.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints after the loss of a lot of blood, he should drink warm broth and subtle aromatic syrup, and use other things that we have said in the division or chapter on syncope, for the opening of the vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to bleed his arm again and again, then when it is weakened by excessive bleeding, he should bleed a little bit at a time according to the amount of his continued strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And those who want to bleed their arms again after the first bleeding, and they have strong bodies, should bleed again after seven hours, or after nine hours.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wants to bleed elsewhere, it must bleed on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is much blood within the body which has been heated, and fever arises; therefore one must draw off a large quantity, and widen the vein until it drips gently; then you should check all the conditions of bleeding, and put your hand on his pulse while he bleeds, so that death does not come from the place of the vein, and this happens many times when the surgeon is negligent; and one must not press hard on the vein when you see the arm loosening and bleeding for a second time, and the vein is closed, but one should press gently; nor if it is crooked, should he stretch out his arm forcefully, for that would be bad; but let him remain as he is while he bleeds for a second time; or one should apply the point of the cautery flame until the congealed blood at the vein opening melts away, and put a little salt dissolved in water on it, and press gently.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	If a vein is swollen, leave it and do not constrict it until the abscess has been drained.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	If necessary, bleed a second time in the same vein, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	Veins in the arm are bled in the area of the vein in the head because it is more complex.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of bleeding is that the patient puts his hand in hot water until the vein turns red; then let it be handled gently so that the vein appears clearly, then bleed now from the side, not from the top or bottom; and make the cut wide, and bleed close to the joint of the hand, and if blood cannot come out, put the hand back in hot water and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough; and if it is in the winter, do not put the hand back in hot water, because it is put in more in the winter than in the summer; and bleeding from this vein is safer than from any other vein, as there are no arteries or nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	Bleeding the救命 vein of the right hand is beneficial for all liver diseases, and this is how it is done: stretch out the hand, and put it in hot water until the vein swells, which one can see; then bleed from the side, and if you close it completely, it will do no harm; and do not go too deep because the nerves are completely naked beneath the skin. Then put the hand back in hot water if the blood congeals in the wound and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as needed, put oil and silk on the vein to seal it quickly, and do the same for each vein.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The bleeding in the left hand is beneficial for the disease of the right side, and do everything as I have told you for the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The medicine of the sophia is good for all diseases that are under the body, such as diseases of the stomach, and retention of fluids, and diseases of the kidneys, and the thighs and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the qualities of its medicine are such that the patient puts his foot in hot water, and rubs on the vein until it breaks, and applies it to the joint of the foot; and if the vein is at the ankle, and up the foot, they go a lot of rains; therefore heal it at the largest vein, or at the ankle, which heals better.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you heal it on the foot, then beware of the nerves that are underneath, and heal it across as well by coping; and let the flames be ανέσυλη.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, then put the foot in water, and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the healer fails the first time, then he should try again the second time above a little, because the place is salty; do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and thus do with the sophia of the other foot similarly.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The site of the sciatic vein is at the ankle, and its cure lies in the pain of the hip when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of its healing is that the patient enters the bath, and twists the ankle three times upwards, for otherwise the vein does not open; and if it opens, then heal it in every way you can, and by crossing over; and it is better to cover it, for the part is safe, and it is very relaxed in many people.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not wash it, then heal any vein that opens on the back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and be careful of the nerves; and make the blood flow until you see it, and then loosen the bandage, and put on cotton and compress it; it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	of cupping treatments
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Leches are made of horns, or iron, or glass; and bleeding is done according to 2 methods: either by piercing and drawing blood, or without piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping which is done by burning is in two ways: with fire or without fire; and the cupping that is done by burning and by bloodletting is performed in 14 places on the body, of which one is entirely at the top of the head; and the other is in the neck; and two others are on either side of the neck; and the cupping under the chin; and the cupping on both shoulders; and the cupping over the hips; and the cupping among the two arms; and the cupping on the two legs; and the cupping on the two ankles; and the cupping is not performed for bloodletting, except for small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and because of this it does not weaken at all, as with bloodletting from a vein; and it should not be administered, neither with fire nor without fire, in any disease that comes from fullness, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if, due to necessity or habit, one must bleed, then we treat them every hour at the beginning or end of the month, in summer and in every season; for there are some who, when they need to bleed, feel a heavy head; and there are some who experience fullness and redness in their face, head, and neck, and darkness in their eyes; and some who experience a drop of blood in their mouth, have a swollen tongue, and taste blood; and there are those who faint, see things that are not there, and experience pain and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, especially when it is during the month, we command them to fast after 3 hours in the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The bleeding of the nose helps with headaches ... that come to the eyes, and it must not be after the evacuation of the whole body; and this bleeding is in the place of the cephalic, and one who has a cold complexion or catarrh should not use it, for it does them great harm; and therefore the old should not use it, nor those who have cold diseases in their head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often heal from it become oblate, and for this reason the cupping should be placed a little lower down due to the risk of oblateness.Car li veillart et cil qui ont chief froides maladies, si conviennent que les ventoses soient plus avals sur la cephalique, car ce lor fait grant bem;
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The ventilation in the neck is located where the jugular vein and basilic vein are, and because of this, it helps with constriction of the foot, and with splitting of the channels of the lungs, and with vomiting, and with repletion; and one should not push on it too much, for if it is pressed too firmly, it affects the throat and stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The ventilations at the sides of the neck help with headache and eye pain and migraine, and with strangulation, and with toothache, and they are located where the basilic vein is; and you should instruct the surgeon to express his hand when placing it, so that he does not compress the artery and cause a flow of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	Ventilation under the chin is good for mouth diseases and gum corruption and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in the area of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Ventilation on the shoulders is good for diseases that come from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The ventilations in the armpits are like three veins in the arm, for they draw blood from those large veins; and command the surgeon not to pierce too deeply, for under the skin there are nerves and arteries.Li ventosation dou chef alerge tant a l’estrecement des ners com a la sainie de la veine dou chief; et est as III costelz, et covient que li sainors si mette le doigt et li tienne fermement, qu’il ne se mueve.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping glass that is placed on the buttock is useful for hemorrhoids and other diseases underneath, and it should be large, made of brass, and well-suctioning; and by chance, if it is fragile, it may break and cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	Cupping glasses on the legs heal very well, as they draw blood from the whole body; and they are useful for old pains in the kidneys, and for diseases of the stomach, and of the bladder, and they bring relief to flowers; and they are located at the .2nd sophene, and at the .2nd ankle, and all the while they weaken the body after a long time, and bring on fainting in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of applying the cupping glass is to place it first empty, and suck gently, and apply firmly, and move evenly, and do not cease doing this until you see the spot red and swollen, and the blood appears; then stop, and remove the cups, and take care in the disposition of the body, for there are those who have thin skin and wide pores: one must strike only once, and one must make large wounds, and a little deep; and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, then one must strike twice: the first time to subtilize the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, then one must strike a third time; and when we want to draw blood a little at a time, we only need to strike once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want a lot of blood, we will re-bleed frequently; and if the blood is thick, pierce it with a needle, and the areas where the veins are to be pierced suddenly, and it suits those who have tough and hard skin and narrow pores that you grease the ends of the cupping glasses with aperitif and dissolutive oil: if it is in the summer, with violet oil, or with sweet almond oil, or with squash seed oil; and if it's winter, use watercress oil, or lily, or chamomile, or similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the suppuration is thick and cold, then take marigold oil, or balsamite oil, or dill oil, and similar oils.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the patient has tender skin and wide pores, no oil is needed, but it should be washed after cupping with rosewater, or cold water, or mulberry water, or squash water, or porcelain water, or similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have a lot of moisture should also use parsley, or water from the myrtle tree, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have large swollen areas are raised by old wine, or by water of suc, or by decoction of aniseed or chamomile, or other similar things; and it is not good to bleed with a cupping glass before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two; and do not sleep after being bled, and they must keep themselves warm when they are being bled and when they have been bled.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And watch if the person who is being bled is colicky, and if the blood is too thin and inflamed; then they should eat cool things such as pomegranates and endives and lettuce with garlic, and similar things; and soft foods, and the flesh of young animals, and moist foods.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those with a cold complexion should drink honey syrup, and moderately old but not too old wine, which is between old and new, and soft foods, and soft young birds and pigeons; and on the day that they are bled, they should drink more than they eat; and it is good to give some people rose water or musk rose water before or after bleeding to comfort the main organs; and the blood should be thin but not for those who have a hot complexion.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The cupping glasses that are placed without burning are those that are placed on the liver, and on the mumps, and on the gout, and on the belly, and the groin, and the thighs, and the hip; for these members do not bear to be burned, and it is only done in order to attract blood from one member to another, as we place them on the breasts when the nipples are healthy; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we place cupping glasses on the belly and on the groin to reduce the member; and it removes pain when there is congestion or a stone, and by its attractive power it may draw out the congestion, or drive away the stone from its place; and thus it acts when one places it on the liver and on the mumps when there is retained flatulence, and these cupping glasses are administered empty in order to suck only; and sometimes they are administered with fire, and sometimes filled with warm water, as in diseases of the pleurisy, and in this way one fills the cupping glass with hot water alone, or with water in which suitable herbs have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the fire cupping is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it is two fingers wide and a half palm deep, and on the sides around the middle there is a small hole, as well as for pushing a needle, and it should be made of bronze, smooth in front so that it does not hurt the patient when placed on the limb; and in the middle there is a crossbar of bronze or iron, to place a candle, and they are large and small according to the illnesses and the age of those who take them; for the ventouses of children are different from the old, and of the thin from the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one should thus place this ventouse on the limb: take the candle of wax or the ointment, and place it within the ventouse through the bar in the middle of the ventouse, so that the light is at the bottom of the ventouse and does not burn the patient; and then place it on the limb, and your fingers must be on the hole we mentioned, so that when one wishes, the vapor goes out, and one removes the ventouse; and they take the ointment as before, and repeat it often if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	Therefore the cupping-glass which is applied for the disease of pleurisy, for all acute diseases, has no rod nor aperture, and it is not removed until it is full of water, and is placed on the limb only; and that is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Leeches are not removed until they are in fresh, clear water without any dirt, and they are put only on members where cupping-glasses cannot be used because of their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar places; and on bare flesh, such as the teeth or nose, and others like them; and the way to use them is that when you find leeches which are in clear, fresh water without any dirt, you take them; and put one in clear water, until they become accustomed and have nothing in their guts; and then let it be bled from a vein and cupped, then rub the member until it turns red, and put the leeches on it; and when they are full and move, if it is a place where a cupping-glass can be used, let it be used, for that is much better.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, then lift the place with ash, and then with water, very well, and then squeeze it out; and if the vein heals too close to the body of the leech, moisten a linen cloth in cold water, and apply it so that the leech is constricted; and if the bleeding increases, then apply powdered vitriol, or gall, and similar things, until it is stopped; or place half a handful of peas over the spot, and leave them until they turn green on the spot, and it will now stop; and if you need more, take other leeches.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the leeches will not attach, then rub the bleeding spot with fresh blood, or prick it with a needle so that the blood flows, and then apply them, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will attach; and when you see that they are defecating, then powder over the spot some powdered aloes and salt, or ashes, and they will stop now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine and is a remedy for fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that the fools who despise this chapter have never seen any of the ancient books or read any letters; and because of this, knowledge is strange in our land, for I have never found any good ones. And I know nothing except through the knowledge of ancient books, in which I have studied so much that I have gained knowledge, and through experiment and the custom of my life. And I have described to you in this chapter what is contained in it, and I have abbreviated it at the end, and I have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, just as I did in the two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, we should say in the prologue of this book the subjects of the discourse and the chapters where the sage sets his understanding, and dwells on their truth, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twisting or crushing occurs in someone, you should quickly treat the patient from one side and the other, if nothing else prevents it, such as weakness of the body, or old age, or being very cold; or if the weather is very hot or too cold. Eat cool foods, that is, cold meats, and deer and squirrel meat, and do not drink wine or eat any fatty foods, and do not fill yourself with food that fills the veins with blood, until you have thought of a hot abscess, or of an expansion of matter in the limb; then let the patient return to their previous diet.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, then one should nourish the patient with foods that promote swelling, or have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, and rice, and testicles, and feet, and cow's placenta, and offal, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with such swelling the fracture is stopped up and heals more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that broken bones in the old and decrepit cannot be well healed or joined according to their nature due to the dryness of the limbs, nor those that are also too tender, such as the bones of young children; but have no care, reset the broken bone, binding it tightly with large tendons that stretch and join the limb together, so that it is as forced as it was before; and do not stop at all in his work, and for this he should eat plenty of meat, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And you should know that there are various types of fractures in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot or leg; and I will tell you in this chapter about all types of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes to the bone, and another one that is superficial, just like the cut of a quill pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there is a fracture with a wound, and a complete fracture is a small split.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And for each type there is its own technique and proper instrument in the restoration, according to what the memory comes to mind; and one can tell that the bone is broken when it is twisted, and clearly appears deformed, and buzzes when pressed by the hand; and when there is no twisting or deformity, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no fracture; but there may be a twisting, or splitting, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	You must not move it by hand, but apply remedies that follow, then hold it steady with a gentle grip.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And you should know that the fracture which goes towards the root, and where the two parts are separated, they must now be put back together evenly, so that hot abscesses can form; and if cold abscesses form, then leave it for a day, until the abscess is relieved; then put it back into alignment as easily and quickly as you can, and know that the restoration of this one is easier than the restoration of the one where there are pieces; then hold it tight, as it should be done afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if there are broken pieces of bone, whether it be in two parts, or in the hand or foot, or in your hand if it is a small member, or in two tendons, or in one tendon and your hand; and put the member back into its natural shape, so that when the broken parts of the member are separated, you bring them back together by all means possible, and be careful that your work does not cause injury or pain to the patient; and adjust the two heads of the bone according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it with your hand if it does not seem right; then adjust it well, and do not pull or press too hard as those do who cause hot abscesses and contractions in the member through their actions, as we have seen many times.Et s’il est desaloiee par cause de moistor ou de fureur, si le ramene en sa leu, et il ne puet y demorer, si le remet a leu si com il doit etre;
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the member is at its worst, then treat the patient well so that he does not move it, either while awake or sleeping, turning or in any other way; and be careful that the member is so secure that he feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, then it is not at its worst, and you should put him in such a position that he feels no pain; and be careful that he is straightened out, so that no crookedness comes to him when he is restored; and the quality of the broken member is according to what I have told you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken members vary in size, shape, and form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Because there are small members, like arms and fingers and the like: these should be wrapped with soft, fine linen; and for larger ones, such as thighs and legs, use a broad, sturdy bandage, since broad bandages embrace all of the large member and constrict it evenly from all sides, so that no swelling remains; then wind soft pads around it, three or four times according to the size of the member, and press your hand gently on all of the bandage, then go above the break and constrict it less, until the break recedes a little; then soften the bandage little by little, until you hold most of the healthy part, then take another bandage and wind it again around the broken part; then go back to the part below the break and constrict it gently, neither too hard nor too softly, as we have said above in the first hour; then place pads or linen between the bandages, until they are all even, then bind everything on top with a bandage, and then put your splints well-made on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or an abscess, apply something hot that soothes the abscess and reduces the swelling; leave it like this for several days. Then, place it over a fire, and let it be of half the thickness of a large cane, or of wood used for making clubs, or of palm tree branches, and let it be shaped thus:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But the splint that one puts on the fracture should be a little thicker and wider than the others; it should also be as long as necessary for the smallness or size of the limb; then tighten it over the splints just as you did at first, and then tie a thread over it appropriately, just as in the case of the first fracture; the tighter it is, the better; and the threads should be thin, neither too thick nor too fine, and they should be made of soft flax; for if the threads are thick, as I have seen foolish people make their laces with twisted cords, it is a great error, for the binding cannot be equal if it is too thin.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is wounded on the head by the stars after the binding, place underneath woolen or linen bandages so that it does not blister.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is accompanied by a fracture, and the bones are broken, I will describe the treatment below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And you should not attempt to straighten all the broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the member is swollen, it should not be bandaged for more than five or seven days, or longer depending on the heat of the abscess; and here is the method of ancient poultices for healing fractures, dislocations, and twists: take flour from the walls of the mill and mix it with abundant egg, and apply this preparation, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it. This is the common method of poultice that heals fractures in various conditions, and especially in women and small children, for it is not too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plaster to restore the fracture and dislocation and twisting: take 3 parts rose oil, 1 part each of myrrh and aloe, 8 parts alechi, and in powder, mix with egg white; if the person's complexion is hot, use this plaster, as it has a good composition and restores broken bones quickly, and is suitable for many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method of poultice that is good for twists: take mastic and balsam of galahad, each 10 grams; myrrh and aloes, each 7 grams; açafrão, 6 grams; Armenian bole, 10 grams, and grind well, and mix with water or abundant egg, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another method of ointment for joints and bones dislocated from their places, and to soothe the resulting pain, and to reduce swelling and Bruchure: take new lamb's wool, and moisten it in vinegar and oil, and apply it to the affected area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This ointment does not cure, but it is good for soothing a hot abscess and removing pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of plaster that heals broken bones: take dry fig leaves and deadnettle leaves, and grind them together, and make a plaster from it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of ointment to restore a broken bone and to reduce the remainder of an abscess: take equal parts of honey, wax, and oil, and cook them together.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take the root of marshmallow, camomile, violet flowers, and wheat flour, in equal parts; grind them and cook with wine. If the member is inflamed, cook with water or moist coriander water, and apply it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another more powerful method of ointment when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the limb: take equal parts of honey, wax, and oil, and cook them together. Then add one part each of root of marshmallow, camomile, violet flowers, and wheat flour; grind and cook with vinegar. If the member is inflamed, cook with water or moist coriander water, and apply it.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take the roots of viscovary, and flax seed, borage, melilot, and sanser, and flowers of violets and camomile, of each one part; bruise them, and cook with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hypocras says in his book that one should not put anything on the broken member to restore it other than a cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says that it should be between soft and too hard.Et dist qu’on doit prendre la cerote en la meine et la mettre sus le membre, et la faire adurer a la manie dou feu, si come l’huile chaude, et la mettre sus la brisure.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to Galen that one must put on the broken member, in order to restore, dry things a little warm, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way of ointment that is good for injury and pain: take mugwort and human hair, or bird feathers, and beaver castoreum, and mix them together, and grind them up, and make an ointment out of it, and apply it to the affected area.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then loosen it a little after, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor that the bone moves from its place; if not, loosen it by hand for several days. And if pain comes to the spot, or itching, with rest or swelling, then hurry and loosen it, and remove the ointment immediately; and take light cloth, and sponge of sea moistened, and dip in water, and lift up the spot until the itching ceases and the pain is appeased; then let the member rest for an hour, then place on dry linen, moistened with water or rose oil, and bind it with a bandage, so that you are sure of hot abscess; and let the inflammation of the member subside, and the pain be removed, then begin the subtle binding again, and a little ointment, and do not tighten it as much as before; and subtly until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the hot abscess is red and painful and swollen all around, and you need ointment and binding, then restart it, just as you did at first.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if nothing comes to the member of what we have said, do not release it until after three or four or five or seven days; and sometimes he leaves it for twenty days, according to what one sees, until the fracture heals, and the adjustment of the flesh on top approaches; then restrain it more than before, and increase his food, as I have said before; and if you see the place drying out more than is necessary, know that nourishment cannot come there; therefore moisten it with warm water every time you release it, and do this every third day, and loosen the bandage a little; through this work, therefore, nourishment comes to the member, and it quickly heals what the foolish doctor does, who restores the member crookedly: this is bad, and such work is cowardly, and I see nothing in it but fatigue and doing it properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various breaking methods
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many types of fractures, with various shapes and distinct causes. Some fractures are caused by the impact of a sword, breaking the bone all the way to the joint located under the bone, similar to how a halberd or polearm would strike. This type of fracture is called a "halberd fracture".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword cuts into the bone without piercing it, and this type of fracture is called "absolute"; and the wound from these two fractures is large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a closed fracture, or a split, or from the collarbone, or from falling on stone, or from other similar causes.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a deep fracture that approaches the membrane below the bone, or it is on top of the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound is placed in the bone as finely as a hair, and the split is small, then this type of fracture is called "capillary". And if the wound is caused by a stone, or by falling, or by a similar object, and it pushes the bone fragment inward, and the site is chapped like a blacksmith when they work on kettles; then the stone enters inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more often to those with soft bones in their heads, like children's skulls; and it happens with all types of fractures where small fragments are displaced, as I will explain later.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all types of fractures through examination, and through the corruption that is on them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary appearance is known by the fact that when one has uncovered the bone and rubbed it with a finger, the fracture appears black.Si li os est fraiz et tuit contuz, et n’a nul semblant de brisure, ne conoissons pas s’il y a brisure si nous ne veons la sanguine qui s’en va ou s’en vient; car la sanguine qui s’en va, ne li dislocatiers ne se guarient si tost.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, be wary of signs of infection in the patient, and if you see any malicious accident, such as vomiting bile, loss of consciousness, swelling, fever, eyes bulging and reddening, and other similar signs in various dispositions, then it cannot heal without doubt.Et si li os est contuz et rompu, et li brisure n’est point noire ne sanguine ne s’en va; et les accidens dou malaide ne sont pas sus; et li os est en son leu, et la dislocation est guariee, si covient que tu esprouves li os se il est tuit en son leu; car il adonques n’y a nul semblant de brisure, si li os est contuz.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a dreadful accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the child comes to you for the first time, and it is in winter, then you must remove the tooth before the fourteenth day that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in the spring, then you must hurry to remove the tooth before the seventh day, otherwise, the gum under the tooth will be corrupted and the accidents that we have described will occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of the bone comes just to the membrane that covers the brain, then you should split the split part thus: and it is that you grasp the head of the wounded, and uncover on the bone in all the ways you can, and on the shape of the wound more gently than you can, and if bleeding occurs when uncovering the bone, or a hot abscess, use the help of what is appropriate, and it is that you fill the place with wet bandages in rose oil; and let the wound rest until the hot abscesses are soothed, and be sure of bleeding; then begin around the bone to remove, and it is done according to two ways of work: one way is that you cut closely in front, and this is the shape:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then cut another larger slit than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is to have various slits, some narrow and some wide, pointed, and made of iron; and work gently so you do not cut the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and protruding, you must pierce around it so that you can administer cauteries with tongs without breaking through the bone into the chest cavity; above the tip there should be a rim or a ring that prevents the tip from going beyond the bone. You should have several of these, so that each one goes in at the level of the thickness of the bone, and you will need tongs for all parts of the body. There are three types of tongs:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The technique for piercing around a broken bone is to place one tong on the bone and twist it with your fingers until you feel that the bone is pierced; then move the tong to another spot a little further along, and do this all around. Then cut away the bone between the piercings as precisely and gently as you can, as we have said, until you can pull the bone out by hand or with instruments such as pliers or tweezers; be careful not to touch the brain or the sinuses.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and cut the bone, then it is appropriate to resect the hardness that is left of the bone with any other instrument similar to a chisel, but it should be more blunt and more subtle than the other chisel; and if anything of the small bones or any scales remain, gently remove them with the instruments; then treat the wound with tenting and poultices as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of treatment is that which Galen speaks of, which is safer; he praises it highly, and it is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	First, you should expose a part of the bone where the fracture is open, so that when you have exposed that part, you will place under the head of this lens-shaped instrument, of which there is one made especially for this purpose:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, and the part is painful on both sides, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then tap gently with a small mallet, so that you slightly strike the bone all around, and be careful of the membrane which is underneath; if it is adherent to the bone, loosen it gently, for it can be loosened without harm, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not penetrate to the membrane, and the bone is cut only slightly on top, and there are small pieces, then you should smooth that roughness, and remove the shards with a thin rasp, of which you should have various quantities, in order to apply in each place what is most appropriate, according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	Take the largest rasp first, then one that is more subtle, and do not cease to do so until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other subtle hair-like fractures and breaks, you should treat according to its nature; and this is something that has not been handed down to one who has devoted his studies to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the abscess is exposed, you should take a piece of linen according to the size of the wound and moisten it in rosemary oil, and place it over the wound; then take another piece of linen doubled into two or three layers, soak it in wine and rosemary oil, and place it over the first piece of linen; do this as gently as you can so that you do not put pressure on the abscess, then administer more medicine afterwards through another layer, without squeezing it harder than it covers the wound only; leave it like this for one or two days until the abscess is soothed, then remove it and apply healing medicines such as roots of lilies, and bran, and incense powder, and aristologist, and similar things; make a powder from these ingredients and apply it to the wound, and afterwards administer medicine without biting; and watch that the wound is clean, so you do not leave any ointment behind, nor allow pus to accumulate, for when pus accumulates on the membrane of the brain, it hardens and causes great harm to the patient; because when one applies something biting to the abscess, it softens from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, if any bad accident happens to the patient, as we have said, without a doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if blackness does not come about due to the medicine that has been applied, because of its power, one should take a portion of honey and three parts rose oil and glue it onto a piece of cloth, and apply it to the ulcer; then heal it in ways that are appropriate until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.
