And if it is stuck, especially if both jaws are together, then use hot water and oil, gently massaging until they loosen; do not try to force them open, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought back into alignment and the mouth of the patient is closed tightly without softening, then place moistened dressings made of rose oil and wax on it, and then bind it gently with soft bonds; and let the patient sleep on his back, and let his head be propped up between two cushions so that he does not move it to the right or left, nor does he exert himself to yawn, but takes in only small amounts of food until the pain is gone and the jaw is healed; and then let him eat what he wants easily, and do not make him open his mouth to eat and drink until the jaw is well healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be reset in an hour and are not converted to their place, then fever and usual sickness come, and perhaps stomach upset, and perhaps vomiting clear fluid.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a bad omen; and many die from it within eight days.
de la forcelle	of the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The shoulder cannot be dislocated from the ribcage within its continuance, and it is sometimes dislocated by force, and one feels it well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is that the patient lies down on his back and extends his arms; then press the dislocated area firmly with your palm, and it will return to place; then apply the plaster and bandage, and tie it tightly; and the shoulder joint, which is near the neck, cannot be dislocated; if it does dislocate, and if it returns to place once, then you must put it back in its place, as we have said; then apply the plaster and bandage, and tie it tightly, and instruct the patient to rest until he is healed; and thus is the shoulder joint put back in its place when it has been dislocated.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Know that the shoulder can be dislocated in three ways: one is when it dislocates at the bottom part near the armpit; the second is at the foot part; and sometimes it dislocates at the top part, and this happens rarely; it does not dislocate at the back of the shoulder, nor inside for the nerves; and often it dislocates beneath toward the armpit, especially in those who are thin, but in those who are sturdy, it dislocates with a push, and goes back in with a push.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes it happens to some men that they have a concussion or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think it is dislocated because of that.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Then you must test it until you are certain of it, and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And you will know it is dislocated when it is down toward the armpit, and there is a marked difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one; and you will find a visible difference between them; and you will find a hollow at the top of the shoulder, and beneath the armpit the top of the shoulder, just as if it were an egg; and the patient cannot bring his hand to his nose, nor move in any way; and likewise, if it is dislocated upward, it is not hidden, for you will see it clearly at the touch; and this type of dislocation is not difficult to fix when it is new, or if the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is for the assistant to lift the ill hand upward, then place your fingers under the shoulder joint and lift the joint forcefully upwards into place; while the assistant lifts the hand and extends it upward, then lowers it; this will bring quick relief.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said within a few days, then the patient should be bathed in warm water; and administered softening and soothing ointments, such as decoctions of hellebore, fenugreek, and sweet-robin in water, and be rubbed down; then the patient should lie on their back, and under the affected shoulder a layer of woolen cloth, neither too soft nor too hard, then the minister places their heel on the cloth, and gently lifts the top of the shoulder, and pulls the hand of the affected arm; while another minister holds the head of the affected side so it does not move downward; in this way the shoulder will return immediately, and if you see that it is not returning, do it according to this method: and have a man present who is larger than the patient; and stand straight toward the affected side, and press the healthy shoulder under the affected one, and lift up the cloth so that the patient hangs in the air; and another minister pulls the hand of the affected arm downward toward the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	If the patient is too light, they can be weighed down with something heavy, and the dislocation will return immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And it is reset in another way: a long stick is thrust into the ground, so that the shoulder joint is as warm as a pistol, neither too hot nor too cool; then the patient is placed on top of it, but with a soft cloth underneath, and the patient should be upright; then his hand is extended down on the other side, and the joint will return to its place immediately; and if it does not return by all these things that we have said, then do this cure: take a stick two arms long and four fingers wide, which has a rounded head to easily enter under the shoulder, according to this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then tie it to the top of the shoulder with soft cloth so that the shoulder does not hurt the patient, then place it under the dislocation; and extend his arm along the length of the stick, and tie the shoulder to the stick, and the arm at the hand, then place the arm on .i. plank that is broad, and extend the hand downward, and let the body hang from the other side: the joint will return now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, however it may be, you should then place a woolen sphere underneath the dislocation, then apply the prepared plaster of mill-powder, with incense and egg white, over the entire shoulder and around it; then tighten it under the dislocation gradually, and tie the bandage over the plaster, and hug his hand to his neck, and let his hand remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he eats little, as long as the member is comfortable, because he will heal faster; and then eat more after five or seven days, and move it; and if it is stiff and not softened, then it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint has come out of place because of moisture that it received, or for another reason, then you must administer cauteries to three holes, as it is described in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it dislocates after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot lift his arm upstream, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be fitted into its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Dislocations that are towards the bottom, and in the breasts, or behind, are made by pushing and stretching with the hands, and one administers it elsewhere; and treat it until it is healed.Li dislocation qui sunt devers lou costé, ou en l’espaule, et li mameles, si est par impulsion et estendement, et on li met le membre sur son leu, et il se tient; et si ne se tient, adonc covient que tu remets li membre en son leu.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing, there is stiffness in the limb, and with time and movement, the patient uses the bath many times until the stiffness is alleviated and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of dislocation from the shoulder
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	You should know that the joint of the shoulder is dislocated by the fingers, and it returns with the fingers; and if it is dislocated from all sides, especially in front and behind, and the dislocation is not reduced, for one can see and feel it well, and it dislocates according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sickly neck with the healthy one, you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is crooked, and he cannot bend his arm or touch his shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And you must reset it as soon as abscesses form there, for if abscesses form there, then resetting it will be painful; and by chance it may not be able to be fully reset, especially when it is in the back; so it is worse than other dislocations, and causes greater pain, and by chance death can come.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is, when it can be reset, that you stretch out his hand with your two hands; and let his arms be spread out, and his hands bent according to the elbow, from the inside and outside, and push the joint on his wrists together, or at the root of his palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in the front, then it will return when he bends his hand to his hand and pushes from the root of the palm the elbow which has become dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if he does not want to return to the place, then strong extension is administered; and while two ministers extend the arm, a third minister bends it, so that it does not move at the extension; then the arm is turned from each side, after which you have wrapped a long and wide cloth around it; and when they have joined the joint with their hand, they smear some oil on it to soften the joint, then they push the joint firmly back into place, until it returns; and when it is in place, they apply a dry plaster with egg white, and stretch it firmly, and then let the arm hang from the neck of the sickly one, and leave it for several days, after which they loosen it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, loosen the bandage and leave it; and if you see that the joint is not healing well, restart the poultice and the bandage, and leave it for several days, until it is firmly in place; then loosen it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels soreness after the joint is moved, and it moves, then bath and rub it well, and press until it is soothed; or you put a fat sheep's tongue on the joint, then leave it for one day and one night, then remove it, and make him enter the bath; and when he sweats, gently rub the joint, then put the tongue back on, and then enter the bath again; do this two or three times until he is healed; and if you see fit, put warm cow dung on it with butter, and press it on; it will return to its proper state.
li dislocation de la main	dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The dislocation of the hand is a light injury compared to other joints; nonetheless, it must be put back into place immediately, in the same hour that it was dislocated, especially if the joint is swollen or a hot abscess has formed.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And for the movements, you place the patient's hand on a table, and extend his hand, and look at it to ensure it is straightened, then he places his palm on the appearance of the joint, and bends it until it returns to its normal state; you should also check that it is in its proper position; next, have the patient place the back of his hand on a table while you extend and move it.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, let the patient put the back of his hand on the table, and the surgeon put his hand over that appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it pops back into place now, that is good. If not, then strain it with soothing poultices for abscesses, and let him stay like that without re-dislocating.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back into place after several days, then let the joint remain crooked; and do not harm the patient in any way as long as the hand is numbed, and do not try to pull anything out: then know that either the nerves or arteries are cut; there is no other remedy but to strain with cautery near the case, and by chance nothing else works.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, then put on the plaster that we have mentioned, then he pulls and leaves it for .v. days, then he loosen and leaves it like that.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is any swelling, then moisten it with warm water, and rub it until it heals.Et s’il est desaloie par cause de l’estrainage, si le met a leu et le frotte et remue ains qu’il soit en son leu, puis il met l’emplaustre sus li chiés, et li remedeit.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the fingers of the handAnd s'il est desaloie par cause de l'estrainage, si le met a leu et le frotte et remue ains qu'il soit en son leu, puis il met l'emplaustre sus li dois, et li remedeit.
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Sometimes it is dislocated on one side of the hand, sometimes on the back of the palm or on the belly; then let the fingers be bent towards the part where it is dislocated; and hold the head of the finger, and bend it towards the part where it is dislocated; and leave it for two days, and then put it back in place that day; and do not bind it as we have said, but loosen it at night, and move it during the day, and repeat this often until it is healed; and do likewise if it is dislocated on the belly of the hand, and do as you did before until it is healed; and do likewise if it is dislocated in another place.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	dislocation of the spine from the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine or neck is dislocated, there is no treatment, for death comes quickly with this injury.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that the evacuations occur without voluntary effort, and he cannot hold them in, and many times a limb becomes paralyzed, either the two hips or the two arms or one; and often the skin changes color in four places; when it happens in the back, it is called "gilbositez": the cure is to find out if the gilbositez began in childhood: if not, there is no cure or healing from it.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from falling or blows or similar things, the ancient books on medicine describe in great detail, but I have abbreviated it according to my understanding, and have devised instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the gilbositez that comes on the front foot, there is no healing; and also that which comes directly on both sides, and cannot be cured except by the one that comes straight on the back, as I said; and it must be that the patient stretches his face in one place equally, and has a bandage underneath him so that he does not slip; then insert a brand at the head into the ground, and another at the feet, and tie a string underneath the sores of the patient, and another at the hips, and at the knees, and at the ankles; and two ministers hold the strings, one at the head and the other at the feet, among the brands; and they are tied well, the brand as we have said, and the minister puts his palms on the spine, until it is restored.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return through this treatment, take a board three feet long, and dig under the wall, and let the patient be on their side, and insert the end of the board under the wall, then place the middle of the board on the spine; and have the patient put their feet on the other end of the board, and press hard, until it returns to its place; and if you see fit, do this while turning the body towards the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And you should drive two spikes into the patient's head at a distance of one cubit from the feet, and two more near the feet, with a palm's width between each spike on top and bottom; and let there be an opening in each spike for the rope to pass through, and secure the spikes firmly in the ground so they do not move; and between each pair of spikes, have a turning spike, over which the ropes will turn, and have two small spikes at each turning point, a palm's width long, to guide the turn; and then tie the cord that is between the nails to the turning point towards the head, and the other cord to the other turning point towards the feet, and everyone in the group turns their turn on all the cords, and the master straightens the spine as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is even, then put on a desiccant poultice with egg white, and then the towels, and then the splint of a board three fingers long, which covers the area of swelling and the healthy part of the spine, then tie it with a bandage, as we have said, and use the subtle numbing medicine until it is healed; and if nothing comes in the end but health, then one must administer softening and soothing medicines, with the splint that we have mentioned earlier; and sometimes one administers a piece of plaster, and sometimes the appearance comes on the back of the spine, and one thinks it is dislocation; and it is the bone that is protruding, and one must not have any presumption about it: for perhaps it would bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	of hip dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder do not become dislocated except as dislocations; and the joint of the hip is dislocated according to four parts: inside and outside, front and back; and most inside, and less dislocated in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of its dislocation within is such that when one joins the affected leg with the healthy one, it is longer and the affected knee appears more than the healthy one, and the affected one cannot bend its knee towards the fire; and the part which is next to it is swollen with a hot abscess due to the shoulder joint of the thigh coming close to it.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him to whom it comes as a defense, is that this event is contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of him who experiences it in front are that his leg is well according to its length; nevertheless, he does not bend the knee without pain, and if one wants him to walk, he cannot, and he retains his urine, and the groin swells, and when he goes, he passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him who experiences it behind are that he cannot bend or straighten his knee, and that leg is more crooked than the other, and the groin is softened, and the head of the thigh is at the place below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The remedies for this kind of dislocation are that you examine whether the dislocation is recent, and it remains according to its condition, then there is no cure; and he must not presume.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And for the one whose dislocation is fresh, and it is of the four kinds of dislocation, you hurry to return the joint, and hold it in place and stretch it out, and move it to the right and left; perhaps it will return, and it does not need another cure.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	If it does not return in this way, then you must prepare the assistant strongly, and extend the leg with both hands, or with one hand tied to the knee; and another assistant extends his hand above so that he presses his hands under his heels, then tighten a cord around the thigh; and another ties the head of the patient; and they all stretch upward and downward at once, so that the patient is lifted off the ground once and remains pendant.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common to the four appearances, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, then you must apply pressure in his likeness When the dislocation is on the hip, you must help the patient onto their healthy side, then place the cord around the root of the thigh, and around the location under the groin; then tighten the cord above towards the groin, and towards the armpit; then another assistant grabs his arms, and hugs the large part of the dislocated thigh, and stretches it forcefully: it will return to its place now; and this type of dislocation is less serious than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot bind it in the manner we have said, then you must tie both feet of the patient together with a strong leather strap around the heels and knees; let the leg of the patient be extended two fingers more than the other; then let him be hung by the head from a pole, and let his arms hang down two cubits long; then command the attendant to grab the top of the thigh, and another attendant to hold the patient's leg tightly, for the joint will return quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is reduced, let the patient lie down as we have said in the one who has gout; then tighten the strap on the leg and the foot; then put two brands, one at the head and one at the feet, then insert the brand between the thighs of the patient with the hand in the form; then wrap moist bandages around it so that it does not scorch the patient; then extend each attendant towards him, and let the surgeon put pressure on the dislocation with his hand.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it comes back, that's good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place him on a table and press him as we have said in the dislocation of the elbow, and lay the patient on his healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, one should stretch out the affected leg gently, and according to what I have said; and the helper puts his weight on the painful shoulder, then presses with the other hand, and pulls downward towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is external, one must not extend the patient downward or lift him up from the ground, but he should be as if his hip were dislocated outward, as we have said about lying on both hips; and he should lie on his face, with the bandage stretched as we have said before, and someone should press upon the joint on the table; and when the patient extends his legs and they are even, then adjust the thighs and apply the plaster, and strain it with a bandage so that the hip does not move; and he should rest for 3 or 4 days, then release him, and apply the plaster again; and if you see that they are even, then strain as before, and let him rest for 3 days; then release him and make him walk well until the limb is healed.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of dislocation of the knee:
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	There are three ways that the knee can be dislocated: that is, inside, outside, and behind; it cannot be dislocated in front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the sign is that you command the patient to bend his leg at the thigh, and if it does not bend at the thigh, you know that he is dislocated; and the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and put your back on his face, and put his foot on your feet; then take his knee in your palms, and pull between your fingers, then bend both sides of the knee smoothly; and another minister extends his foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that he bends his leg at the thigh easily; and put the plaster on, and make the leg warm at the thigh, and let them be glued together for three or four days, then loosen it; and the patient should not work at all, until the limb is healed.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not at all, then administer a strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	Heels are sometimes dislocated, and sometimes completely dislocated, both internally and externally.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and they feel pain in the part where it is dislocated; the movements should be gentle, and one must gently stretch out their hands when it is only dislocated.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is healed from everything, then you should make the patient stand straight, and you grip his leg above the ankle; then pull the foot towards you with your right hand and then with your left hand, twice, then stretch it upwards, and pull up the foot firmly; and do this twice, as we have said, by bending and pulling the foot; if it returns, that is good; if not, then recommence the operation, for it will return; and if it cannot return thus, then make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and fix the strap firmly in the ground between his buttocks, and wind cloth around it so that he does not kick with his feet; then one gripper grips his thigh, and another gripper stretches out the foot to his hands or to the leg, so that he pulls it up against the collar of the foot; then stretch each gripper equally, and let the strap be between the patient's buttocks to hold him when he is stretched; then put the grippers equally on his hands, and another gripper grabs the healthy leg from below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is healed, then put the plaster and bandages on top, and tighten it firmly, and tie the foot to the leg, and be careful of the nerves that are behind the ankle, so that the ligature is not too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the ligature loosens, then tighten it; then untie it after a third or a quarter day, and they should walk within four days; and if they walk before this time, there is no guarantee that they will not relapse.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a hot abscess comes, you must calm it, as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
des dois	of the arms
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the arms are dislocated, they should be gently extended without force, and that is a minor matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any part of the foot, then you should make the patient sit on a flat surface or table upright, and put your foot over what is open in the joints, and then press firmly on the foot until it pops back into place; and when it is even, and there is nothing opening, then put a two-legged board under the sole of the foot, then tighten it firmly, and leave it for three days, then untie it; and let the patient rest until they are healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When injury occurs with dislocation, and one wishes to restore it, many times the patient dies: so do not be presumptuous in the treatment if you are not wise in the art or have not used it for a long time; and if you are not compassionate, merciful, and cautious, do not be rash. And at the beginning use warm abscess-soothing things, and leave the patient in God's hand if you do not see hope of recovery; but when you see hope, then immediately reset the limb so that the warm abscesses may heal; and once the limb is back in place, administer warm abscess-soothing things and treat the wound as it should be treated with drying ointments; and if there is a fracture with dislocation, and broken bones, set the bones and do what we have said for simple injuries. And beware of venturing into fear, according to what I have said, for it will harm you according to your Creator, and for the safety of your arms and body.
Amen	So be it.
